**Lithuania**,[[b]](#cite_note-18) officially the **Republic of Lithuania**,[[c]](#cite_note-19) is a country in the [Baltic region](/wiki/Baltic_region "Baltic region") of [Europe](/wiki/Europe "Europe").[[d]](#cite_note-location-28) It is one of three [Baltic states](/wiki/Baltic_states "Baltic states") and lies on the eastern shore of the [Baltic Sea](/wiki/Baltic_Sea "Baltic Sea"), bordered by [Latvia](/wiki/Latvia "Latvia") to the north, [Belarus](/wiki/Belarus "Belarus") to the east and south, [Poland](/wiki/Poland "Poland") to the south, and the Russian [semi-exclave](/wiki/Exclave "Exclave") of [Kaliningrad Oblast](/wiki/Kaliningrad_Oblast "Kaliningrad Oblast") to the southwest, with a [maritime border](/wiki/Maritime_boundary "Maritime boundary") with [Sweden](/wiki/Sweden "Sweden") to the west. Lithuania covers an area of 65,300 km2 (25,200 sq mi), with a population of 2.89 million. Its capital and largest city is [Vilnius](/wiki/Vilnius "Vilnius"); other major cities include [Kaunas](/wiki/Kaunas "Kaunas"), [Klaipėda](/wiki/Klaip%C4%97da "Klaipėda"), [Šiauliai](/wiki/%C5%A0iauliai "Šiauliai") and [Panevėžys](/wiki/Panev%C4%97%C5%BEys "Panevėžys"). [Lithuanians](/wiki/Lithuanians "Lithuanians") who are the titular nation and form the majority of the country's population, belong to the ethnolinguistic group of [Balts](/wiki/Balts "Balts") and speak [Lithuanian](/wiki/Lithuanian_language "Lithuanian language").

For millennia, the southeastern shores of the Baltic Sea were inhabited by various [Baltic tribes](/wiki/Balts "Balts"). In the 1230s, Lithuanian lands were united for the first time by [Mindaugas](/wiki/Mindaugas "Mindaugas"), who formed the [Kingdom of Lithuania](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Lithuania "Kingdom of Lithuania") on 6 July 1253. Subsequent expansion and consolidation resulted in the [Grand Duchy of Lithuania](/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania "Grand Duchy of Lithuania"), which by the 14th century was the largest country in Europe. In 1386, the Grand Duchy entered into a *[de facto](/wiki/De_facto "De facto")* [personal union](/wiki/Personal_union "Personal union") with the [Crown of the Kingdom of Poland](/wiki/Crown_of_the_Kingdom_of_Poland "Crown of the Kingdom of Poland"). The two realms were [united](/wiki/Union_of_Lublin "Union of Lublin") into the [bi-confederal](/wiki/Confederation "Confederation") [Polish-Lithuanian Commonwealth](/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth "Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth") in 1569, forming one of the largest and most prosperous states in Europe. The Commonwealth lasted more than two centuries, until neighbouring countries gradually [dismantled](/wiki/Partitions_of_Poland "Partitions of Poland") it between 1772 and 1795, with the [Russian Empire](/wiki/Russian_Empire "Russian Empire") annexing most of Lithuania's territory.

Towards the end of [World War I](/wiki/World_War_I "World War I"), Lithuania [declared Independence](/wiki/Act_of_Independence_of_Lithuania "Act of Independence of Lithuania") in 1918, founding the modern Republic of Lithuania. In [World War II](/wiki/World_War_II "World War II"), Lithuania was occupied [by the Soviet Union](/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_the_Baltic_states_(1940) "Soviet occupation of the Baltic states (1940)"), [then by Nazi Germany](/wiki/German_occupation_of_Lithuania_during_World_War_II "German occupation of Lithuania during World War II"), before being [reoccupied by the Soviets](/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_the_Baltic_states_(1944) "Soviet occupation of the Baltic states (1944)") in 1944. [Lithuanian armed resistance](/wiki/Lithuanian_partisans "Lithuanian partisans") to the Soviet occupation lasted until the early 1950s. On 11 March 1990, a year before the formal [dissolution of the Soviet Union](/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union "Dissolution of the Soviet Union"), Lithuania became the first Soviet republic to break away when it [proclaimed the restoration of its independence](/wiki/Act_of_the_Re-Establishment_of_the_State_of_Lithuania "Act of the Re-Establishment of the State of Lithuania").

Lithuania is a [developed country](/wiki/Developed_country "Developed country") with a [high income](/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy "World Bank high-income economy") and [an advanced economy](/wiki/Economy_of_Lithuania "Economy of Lithuania"). Lithuania is a member of the [European Union](/wiki/European_Union "European Union"), the [Council of Europe](/wiki/Council_of_Europe "Council of Europe"), the [eurozone](/wiki/Eurozone "Eurozone"), the [Nordic Investment Bank](/wiki/Nordic_Investment_Bank "Nordic Investment Bank"), the [Schengen Agreement](/wiki/Schengen_Agreement "Schengen Agreement"), [NATO](/wiki/NATO "NATO"), and [OECD](/wiki/OECD "OECD"). It also participates in the [Nordic-Baltic Eight](/wiki/Nordic-Baltic_Eight "Nordic-Baltic Eight") (NB8) regional co-operation format.

Etymology
---------

Main article: [Name of Lithuania](/wiki/Name_of_Lithuania "Name of Lithuania")

The spelling of *Lithuania* was a later addition to the original Latinate *Lituania* since 1800 as a form of [hyperforeignism](/wiki/Hyperforeignism "Hyperforeignism") (such as the word *[author](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/author#English "wikt:author")* being a superseding form of older *autor*) influenced by [Greek loanwords](/wiki/English_words_of_Greek_origin "English words of Greek origin") with the [theta](/wiki/Theta "Theta"); it is ultimately from [Lithuanian](/wiki/Lithuanian_language "Lithuanian language"): *Lietuva*.[[25]](#cite_note-29) The first known record of *Lietuva* is in a 9 March 1009 story of [Saint Bruno](/wiki/Bruno_of_Querfurt "Bruno of Querfurt") in the [Quedlinburg Chronicle](/wiki/Quedlinburg_Chronicle "Quedlinburg Chronicle").[[26]](#cite_note-30) The Chronicle recorded a Latinized form of the name Lietuva: *Litua*[[27]](#cite_note-31) (pronounced [litua]). Due to lack of reliable evidence, the true meaning of the name is unknown and scholars still debate it. There are a few plausible versions.[[28]](#cite_note-VardasVle-32)

[Lietava](/wiki/Lietava_River "Lietava River"), a small river not far from [Kernavė](/wiki/Kernav%C4%97 "Kernavė"), the core area of the [early Lithuanian state](/wiki/Duchy_of_Lithuania "Duchy of Lithuania") and a possible first capital of the eventual [Grand Duchy of Lithuania](/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania "Grand Duchy of Lithuania"), is usually credited as the source of the name.[[29]](#cite_note-Zigmas2-33) However, the river is very small and some find it improbable that such a small and local object could have lent its name to an entire nation. On the other hand, such naming is not unprecedented in world history.[[30]](#cite_note-Zigmas-34)

Artūras Dubonis proposed another hypothesis,[[31]](#cite_note-35) that Lietuva relates to the word *[leičiai](/wiki/Lei%C4%8Diai "Leičiai")* (plural of *leitis*). From the middle of the 13th century, *leičiai* were a distinct warrior social group of the [Lithuanian](/wiki/Lithuanians "Lithuanians") society subordinate to the [Lithuanian ruler](/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_Lithuania "List of rulers of Lithuania") or the state itself. The word *leičiai* is used in 14–16th century historical sources as an [ethnonym](/wiki/Ethnonym "Ethnonym") for Lithuanians (but not [Samogitians](/wiki/Samogitians "Samogitians")) and is still used, usually poetically or in historical contexts, in the [Latvian language](/wiki/Latvian_language "Latvian language"), which is closely related to Lithuanian.[[32]](#cite_note-36)[[33]](#cite_note-37)[[34]](#cite_note-38)

History
-------

Main article: [History of Lithuania](/wiki/History_of_Lithuania "History of Lithuania")

### Early history and Baltic tribes

Main article: [Balts](/wiki/Balts "Balts")

See also: [Lithuanian land confederation](/wiki/Lithuanian_land_confederation "Lithuanian land confederation")

The history of Lithuania dates back to settlements founded about 10,000 years ago.[[35]](#cite_note-39)[[36]](#cite_note-kudirka13-40) The first people settled in the territory of Lithuania after the [Last Glacial Period](/wiki/Last_Glacial_Period "Last Glacial Period") in the 10th millennium BC: [Kunda](/wiki/Kunda_culture "Kunda culture"), [Neman](/wiki/Neman_culture "Neman culture") and [Narva cultures](/wiki/Narva_culture "Narva culture").[[37]](#cite_note-PoloméWinter2011-41) They were traveling hunters. In the 8th millennium BC the climate became warmer and forests developed. The inhabitants of what is now Lithuania travelled less and engaged in local hunting, gathering and fresh-water fishing. The [Indo-Europeans](/wiki/Indo-European_migrations "Indo-European migrations"), who arrived in the 3rd – 2nd millennium BC, mixed with the local population and formed various [Baltic tribes](/wiki/Baltic_tribes "Baltic tribes").[[38]](#cite_note-42) The Baltic tribes did not maintain close cultural or political contacts with the [Roman Empire](/wiki/Roman_Empire "Roman Empire"),[[39]](#cite_note-MacDonald1996-43) while maintaining trade contacts via the [Amber Road](/wiki/Amber_Road "Amber Road").

From the 9th to the 11th centuries, coastal Balts were subjected to raids by the [Vikings](/wiki/Vikings "Vikings").[[40]](#cite_note-Kasekamp2017-44) Lithuania comprised mainly the culturally different regions of [Samogitia](/wiki/Samogitia "Samogitia") (known for its early medieval skeletal burials), and further east [Aukštaitija](/wiki/Auk%C5%A1taitija "Aukštaitija"), or [Lithuania proper](/wiki/Lithuania_proper "Lithuania proper") (known for its early medieval cremation burials). The area was remote and unattractive to outsiders, including traders, which accounts for its separate linguistic, cultural and religious identity and delayed integration into general European patterns and trends.[[41]](#cite_note-Ochmański_37-45) Traditional [Lithuanian pagan customs and mythology](/wiki/Lithuanian_mythology "Lithuanian mythology"), with many archaic elements, were long preserved. Rulers' bodies were cremated up until the conversion to Christianity: the descriptions of the cremation ceremonies of the grand dukes [Algirdas](/wiki/Algirdas "Algirdas") and [Kęstutis](/wiki/K%C4%99stutis "Kęstutis") have survived.[[42]](#cite_note-Bumblauskas_24-25-46)

### Kingdom of Lithuania, Grand Duchy of Lithuania and Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth

Main articles: [Duchy of Lithuania](/wiki/Duchy_of_Lithuania "Duchy of Lithuania"), [Kingdom of Lithuania](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Lithuania "Kingdom of Lithuania"), [Grand Duchy of Lithuania](/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania "Grand Duchy of Lithuania"), [Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth](/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth "Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth"), and [Kościuszko Uprising](/wiki/Ko%C5%9Bciuszko_Uprising "Kościuszko Uprising")

The first written record of the name for the country dates back to 1009 AD.[[45]](#cite_note-49) Facing the [German threat](/wiki/Livonian_Crusade "Livonian Crusade"), [Mindaugas](/wiki/Mindaugas "Mindaugas") in the middle of the 13th century united a large part of the [Baltic](/wiki/Balts "Balts") tribes and founded the State of Lithuania, while in 1253 he was crowned as the Catholic [King of Lithuania](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Lithuania "Kingdom of Lithuania").[[46]](#cite_note-Mindaugas-50)[[47]](#cite_note-LTHistoryBritannica-51) Moreover by taking advantage of the weakened territory of the former [Kievan Rus'](/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27 "Kievan Rus'") due to the [Mongol invasion](/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Kievan_Rus%27 "Mongol invasion of Kievan Rus'"), Mindaugas incorporated [Black Ruthenia](/wiki/Black_Ruthenia "Black Ruthenia") into Lithuania.[[46]](#cite_note-Mindaugas-50) After Mindaugas' assassination in 1263, [pagan Lithuania](/wiki/Lithuanian_mythology "Lithuanian mythology") was again a target of the [Christian crusades](/wiki/Lithuanian_Crusade "Lithuanian Crusade") of the [Teutonic Knights](/wiki/Teutonic_Knights "Teutonic Knights") and [Livonian Order](/wiki/Livonian_Order "Livonian Order").[[48]](#cite_note-52) [Traidenis](/wiki/Traidenis "Traidenis") during his reign (1269–1282) reunified all Lithuanian lands and achieved military successes against the Crusaders, fighting alongside other Baltic tribes, but was unable to militarily assist the [Old Prussians](/wiki/Old_Prussians "Old Prussians") in their [Great Uprising](/wiki/Prussian_uprisings#The_Great_Prussian_uprising_(1260–1274) "Prussian uprisings").[[49]](#cite_note-Traidenis-53) Traidenis' main residence was in [Kernavė](/wiki/Kernav%C4%97 "Kernavė").[[49]](#cite_note-Traidenis-53)

From the late 13th century members of the [Lithuanian](/wiki/Lithuanians "Lithuanians") [Gediminids](/wiki/Gediminids "Gediminids") dynasty began ruling Lithuania, who consolidated a [hereditary monarchy](/wiki/Hereditary_monarchy "Hereditary monarchy") and the [status](/wiki/Letters_of_Gediminas "Letters of Gediminas") of [Vilnius](/wiki/Vilnius "Vilnius") as permanent [capital city](/wiki/Capital_city "Capital city"), [christianized Lithuania](/wiki/Christianization_of_Lithuania "Christianization of Lithuania") and by incorporating [East Slavs](/wiki/East_Slavs "East Slavs")' territories (e.g. principalities of [Minsk](/wiki/Principality_of_Minsk "Principality of Minsk"), [Kyiv](/wiki/Principality_of_Kiev "Principality of Kiev"), [Polotsk](/wiki/Principality_of_Polotsk "Principality of Polotsk"), [Vitebsk](/wiki/Principality_of_Vitebsk "Principality of Vitebsk"), [Smolensk](/wiki/Principality_of_Smolensk "Principality of Smolensk"), etc.) significantly expanded the [Grand Duchy of Lithuania](/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania "Grand Duchy of Lithuania")'s territory, which reached ~650,000 km2 in the first half of the 14th century.[[50]](#cite_note-VleLDK-54) At the end of the 14th century Lithuania was the largest country in [Europe](/wiki/Europe "Europe").[[43]](#cite_note-Bideleux-47)[[44]](#cite_note-USDoS-48) In 1385, Lithuania formed a [dynastic union](/wiki/Dynastic_union "Dynastic union") with [Poland](/wiki/Poland_during_the_Jagiellon_dynasty "Poland during the Jagiellon dynasty") through the [Union of Krewo](/wiki/Union_of_Krewo "Union of Krewo").[[50]](#cite_note-VleLDK-54) Furthermore, in the late 14th–15th centuries [patrilineal](/wiki/Patrilineality "Patrilineality") [members](/wiki/Jagiellonian_dynasty "Jagiellonian dynasty") of the Lithuanian ruling Gediminids dynasty ruled not only Lithuania and Poland, but [Hungary](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary_(1301%E2%80%931526) "Kingdom of Hungary (1301–1526)"), [Croatia](/wiki/Croatia_in_personal_union_with_Hungary "Croatia in personal union with Hungary"), [Bohemia](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bohemia "Kingdom of Bohemia"), and [Moldavia](/wiki/Moldavia "Moldavia").[[51]](#cite_note-55)[[52]](#cite_note-56) The German attacks on Lithuania were ceased with a decisive Polish–Lithuanian victory in the [Battle of Grunwald](/wiki/Battle_of_Grunwald "Battle of Grunwald") in 1410 and by concluding the [Treaty of Melno](/wiki/Treaty_of_Melno "Treaty of Melno") in 1422.[[50]](#cite_note-VleLDK-54)

In the 15th century the strengthened [Grand Duchy of Moscow](/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Moscow "Grand Duchy of Moscow") renewed the [Muscovite–Lithuanian Wars](/wiki/Muscovite%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Wars "Muscovite–Lithuanian Wars") for the Lithuanian-controlled [Eastern Orthodox](/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church "Eastern Orthodox Church") territories.[[50]](#cite_note-VleLDK-54) Due to the unsuccessful beginning of the [Livonian War](/wiki/Livonian_War "Livonian War"), loss of land to the [Tsardom of Russia](/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia "Tsardom of Russia"), and pressure by monarch [Sigismund II Augustus](/wiki/Sigismund_II_Augustus "Sigismund II Augustus"), a supporter of a close Polish–Lithuanian union, the [Lithuanian nobility](/wiki/Lithuanian_nobility "Lithuanian nobility") agreed to conclude the [Union of Lublin](/wiki/Union_of_Lublin "Union of Lublin") in 1569 with the [Crown of the Kingdom of Poland](/wiki/Crown_of_the_Kingdom_of_Poland "Crown of the Kingdom of Poland"), which created a new [federative](/wiki/Federation "Federation") [Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth](/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth "Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth") with a joint monarch (holding both titles of the King of Poland and Grand Duke of Lithuania), but Lithuania remained a separate state from Poland with its own territory (~300 000 km2), coat of arms, management apparatus, laws, courts, seal, army, treasury, etc.[[53]](#cite_note-LUnija-57)[[50]](#cite_note-VleLDK-54) After concluding the [real union](/wiki/Real_union "Real union") Lithuania and Poland jointly managed to reach military successes during the Livonian War, [occupation of Moscow](/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_occupation_of_Moscow "Polish–Lithuanian occupation of Moscow") (1610), [war with Sweden (1600–1611)](/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Swedish_War_(1600%E2%80%931611) "Polish–Swedish War (1600–1611)"), [Smolensk war with Russia (1632–1634)](/wiki/Smolensk_War "Smolensk War"), etc.[[50]](#cite_note-VleLDK-54)[[53]](#cite_note-LUnija-57) In 1588, [Sigismund III Vasa](/wiki/Sigismund_III_Vasa "Sigismund III Vasa") personally confirmed the [Third Statute of Lithuania](/wiki/Statutes_of_Lithuania#Third_Statute "Statutes of Lithuania") where it was stated that Lithuania and Poland have equal rights within the Commonwealth and ensured the [separation of powers](/wiki/Separation_of_powers "Separation of powers").[[54]](#cite_note-58) The real union strongly intensified the [Polonization](/wiki/Polonization "Polonization") of Lithuania and Lithuanian nobility.[[55]](#cite_note-59)

The mid-17th century was marked with disastrous military loses for Lithuania as during the [Deluge](/wiki/Deluge_(history) "Deluge (history)") most of the territory of Lithuania was annexed by the Tsardom of Russia and even Lithuania's capital Vilnius was fully [captured](/wiki/Battle_of_Vilnius_(1655) "Battle of Vilnius (1655)") for the first time by a foreign army and ravaged.[[56]](#cite_note-Raila-60) In 1655, Lithuania unilaterally [seceded](/wiki/Union_of_K%C4%97dainiai "Union of Kėdainiai") from Poland, declared the Swedish King [Charles X Gustav](/wiki/Charles_X_Gustav_of_Sweden "Charles X Gustav of Sweden") as the Grand Duke of Lithuania and fell under the [protection of the Swedish Empire](/wiki/Swedish_Lithuania "Swedish Lithuania").[[57]](#cite_note-61) However, by 1657 Lithuania was once again a part of the Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth following the Lithuanian revolt against the Swedes.[[58]](#cite_note-62) Vilnius was recaptured from the Russians in 1661.[[59]](#cite_note-63)

In the second half of the 18th century the Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth was three times [partitioned](/wiki/Partitions_of_Poland "Partitions of Poland") by three neighboring countries which completely [dissoluted](/wiki/Dissolution_(politics) "Dissolution (politics)") both independent Lithuania and Poland from the political map in 1795 after a failed [Kościuszko Uprising](/wiki/Ko%C5%9Bciuszko_Uprising "Kościuszko Uprising") and short-lived [recapture of capital Vilnius](/wiki/Vilnius_uprising_(1794) "Vilnius uprising (1794)") in 1794.[[50]](#cite_note-VleLDK-54) Most of Lithuania's territory was [annexed by the Russian Empire](/wiki/Russian_Partition "Russian Partition"), while [Užnemunė](/wiki/U%C5%BEnemun%C4%97 "Užnemunė") [[lt](https://lt.wikipedia.org/wiki/U%C5%BEnemun%C4%97 "lt:Užnemunė")] was annexed by [Prussia](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia "Kingdom of Prussia").[[50]](#cite_note-VleLDK-54)

### Efforts to restore statehood

Main articles: [November Uprising](/wiki/November_Uprising "November Uprising"), [January Uprising](/wiki/January_Uprising "January Uprising"), and [Lithuanian National Revival](/wiki/Lithuanian_National_Revival "Lithuanian National Revival")

Following the annexation the [Russian Tsarist](/wiki/Tsarist_autocracy "Tsarist autocracy") authorities implemented [Russification](/wiki/Russification "Russification") policies in Lithuania, which then made a part of a new administrative region [Northwestern Krai](/wiki/Northwestern_Krai "Northwestern Krai").[[61]](#cite_note-Vle1795-1914-65) In 1812 [Napoleon](/wiki/Napoleon "Napoleon") during the [French invasion of Russia](/wiki/French_invasion_of_Russia "French invasion of Russia") has established the puppet [Lithuanian Provisional Governing Commission](/wiki/Lithuanian_Provisional_Governing_Commission "Lithuanian Provisional Governing Commission") to support his war efforts, however after Napoleon's defeat the Russian rule was reinstated in Lithuania.[[61]](#cite_note-Vle1795-1914-65)

During the [November Uprising](/wiki/November_Uprising "November Uprising") (1830–1831) the Lithuanians and Poles jointly attempted to restore their statehoods, however the Russian victory resulted in stricter Russification measures: the [Russian language](/wiki/Russian_language "Russian language") was introduced in all government institutions, [Vilnius University](/wiki/Vilnius_University "Vilnius University") was closed in 1832, and theories that Lithuania had been a "Western Russian" state since its establishment were propagated.[[61]](#cite_note-Vle1795-1914-65) Subsequently, the Lithuanians once again tried to restore statehood by participating in the [January Uprising](/wiki/January_Uprising "January Uprising") (1863–1864), but yet another Russian victory resulted in even stronger Russification policies with the introduction of the [Lithuanian press ban](/wiki/Lithuanian_press_ban "Lithuanian press ban"), pressure on the [Catholic Church in Lithuania](/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_Lithuania "Catholic Church in Lithuania") and [Mikhail Muravyov-Vilensky](/wiki/Mikhail_Muravyov-Vilensky "Mikhail Muravyov-Vilensky")'s repressions.[[61]](#cite_note-Vle1795-1914-65)[[62]](#cite_note-JIB-66)

[Simonas Daukantas](/wiki/Simonas_Daukantas "Simonas Daukantas") promoted a return to Lithuania's pre-Commonwealth traditions, which he depicted as a Golden Age of Lithuania and a renewal of the native culture, based on the [Lithuanian language](/wiki/Lithuanian_language "Lithuanian language") and customs. With those ideas in mind, he wrote already in 1822 a history of Lithuania in Lithuanian – *Darbai senųjų lietuvių ir žemaičių* (*The Deeds of Ancient Lithuanians and Samogitians*), though it was not published at that time.[[63]](#cite_note-67) A colleague of S. Daukantas, [Teodor Narbutt](/wiki/Teodor_Narbutt "Teodor Narbutt"), wrote in Polish a voluminous *Ancient History of the Lithuanian Nation* (1835–1841), where he likewise expounded and expanded further on the concept of historic Lithuania, whose days of glory had ended with the Union of Lublin in 1569. Narbutt, invoking German scholarship, pointed out the relationship between the Lithuanian and Sanskrit languages.[[64]](#cite_note-68)

The Lithuanians resisted Russification through an extensive network of [Lithuanian book smugglers](/wiki/Lithuanian_book_smugglers "Lithuanian book smugglers"), secret Lithuanian publishing and homeschooling.[[65]](#cite_note-69) Moreover, the [Lithuanian National Revival](/wiki/Lithuanian_National_Revival "Lithuanian National Revival"), inspired by Lithuanian history, language and culture, laid the foundations for the reestablishment of an independent Lithuania.[[66]](#cite_note-70) The [Great Seimas of Vilnius](/wiki/Great_Seimas_of_Vilnius "Great Seimas of Vilnius") was held in 1905 and its participants adopted resolutions which demanded a wide [autonomy](/wiki/Autonomy#Politics "Autonomy") for Lithuania.[[61]](#cite_note-Vle1795-1914-65)

### Restored statehood and occupations

Main articles: [Act of Independence of Lithuania](/wiki/Act_of_Independence_of_Lithuania "Act of Independence of Lithuania"), [Occupation of the Baltic states](/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Baltic_states "Occupation of the Baltic states"), [German occupation of Lithuania during World War II](/wiki/German_occupation_of_Lithuania_during_World_War_II "German occupation of Lithuania during World War II"), and [Lithuanian Soviet Socialist Republic](/wiki/Lithuanian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Lithuanian Soviet Socialist Republic")

See also: [Lithuanian partisans](/wiki/Lithuanian_partisans "Lithuanian partisans") and [Guerrilla war in the Baltic states](/wiki/Guerrilla_war_in_the_Baltic_states "Guerrilla war in the Baltic states")

During [World War I](/wiki/World_War_I "World War I") the [German Empire](/wiki/German_Empire "German Empire") annexed Lithuanian territories from the Russian Empire and they became a part of *[Ober Ost](/wiki/Ober_Ost "Ober Ost")*.[[67]](#cite_note-Vle1918-1920-71) In 1907, the Lithuanians organized the [Vilnius Conference](/wiki/Vilnius_Conference "Vilnius Conference") which adopted a resolution, featuring the aspiration for the restoration of Lithuania's sovereignty and military alliance with Germany and elected the [Council of Lithuania](/wiki/Council_of_Lithuania "Council of Lithuania").[[67]](#cite_note-Vle1918-1920-71) In 1918, the short-lived [Kingdom of Lithuania](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Lithuania_(1918) "Kingdom of Lithuania (1918)") was proclaimed; however on 16 February 1918 the Council of Lithuania adopted the [Act of Independence of Lithuania](/wiki/Act_of_Independence_of_Lithuania "Act of Independence of Lithuania") which restored Lithuania as [democratic](/wiki/Democracy "Democracy") [republic](/wiki/Republic "Republic") with its capital in [Vilnius](/wiki/Vilnius "Vilnius") and separated that state from all state relations that existed with other nations.[[67]](#cite_note-Vle1918-1920-71) In 1918–1920 the Lithuanians defended the statehood of Lithuania during the [Lithuanian Wars of Independence](/wiki/Lithuanian_Wars_of_Independence "Lithuanian Wars of Independence") with [Bolsheviks](/wiki/Lithuanian%E2%80%93Soviet_War "Lithuanian–Soviet War"), [Bermontians](/wiki/Lithuanian%E2%80%93Bermontian_War "Lithuanian–Bermontian War") and [Poles](/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_War "Polish–Lithuanian War").[[67]](#cite_note-Vle1918-1920-71) The aims of the newly restored Lithuania clashed with [Józef Piłsudski](/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski "Józef Piłsudski")'s plans to create a [federation](/wiki/Federation "Federation") ([Intermarium](/wiki/Intermarium "Intermarium")) in territories previously ruled by the [Jagiellonians](/wiki/Jagiellonian_dynasty "Jagiellonian dynasty").[[68]](#cite_note-72) The Lithuanian authorities prevented the [1919 Polish coup attempt in Lithuania](/wiki/1919_Polish_coup_attempt_in_Lithuania "1919 Polish coup attempt in Lithuania") and in 1920 during the [Żeligowski's Mutiny](/wiki/%C5%BBeligowski%27s_Mutiny "Żeligowski's Mutiny") the Polish forces captured [Vilnius Region](/wiki/Vilnius_Region "Vilnius Region") and established a [puppet state](/wiki/Puppet_state "Puppet state") of the [Republic of Central Lithuania](/wiki/Republic_of_Central_Lithuania "Republic of Central Lithuania"), which in 1922 was incorporated into Poland.[[67]](#cite_note-Vle1918-1920-71) Consequently, [Kaunas](/wiki/Kaunas "Kaunas") became the [temporary capital of Lithuania](/wiki/Temporary_capital_of_Lithuania "Temporary capital of Lithuania") where the [Constituent Assembly of Lithuania](/wiki/Constituent_Assembly_of_Lithuania "Constituent Assembly of Lithuania") was held and other primary Lithuanian institutions operated until 1940.[[69]](#cite_note-73) In 1923, the [Klaipėda Revolt](/wiki/Klaip%C4%97da_Revolt "Klaipėda Revolt") was organized which unified the [Klaipėda Region](/wiki/Klaip%C4%97da_Region "Klaipėda Region") with Lithuania.[[70]](#cite_note-Vle1920-1940-74) The [1926 Lithuanian coup d'état](/wiki/1926_Lithuanian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "1926 Lithuanian coup d'état") replaced the democratically elected government and [president](/wiki/Kazys_Grinius#President_(1926) "Kazys Grinius") with an [authoritarian](/wiki/Authoritarianism "Authoritarianism") regime led by [Antanas Smetona](/wiki/Antanas_Smetona "Antanas Smetona").[[70]](#cite_note-Vle1920-1940-74)

In the late 1930s Lithuania has accepted the [1938 Polish ultimatum](/wiki/1938_Polish_ultimatum_to_Lithuania "1938 Polish ultimatum to Lithuania"), [1939 German ultimatum](/wiki/1939_German_ultimatum_to_Lithuania "1939 German ultimatum to Lithuania") and transferred the Klaipėda Region to [Nazi Germany](/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany") and following the beginning of the [World War II](/wiki/World_War_II "World War II") concluded the [Soviet–Lithuanian Mutual Assistance Treaty](/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Mutual_Assistance_Treaty "Soviet–Lithuanian Mutual Assistance Treaty").[[71]](#cite_note-VleListorija-75) In 1940 Lithuania has accepted the [Soviet ultimatum](/wiki/Soviet_ultimatum_to_Lithuania "Soviet ultimatum to Lithuania") and recovered the control of historical capital Vilnius, however the acceptance resulted in the [Soviet occupation of Lithuania](/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_the_Baltic_states_(1940) "Soviet occupation of the Baltic states (1940)") and its transformation into the [Lithuanian Soviet Socialist Republic](/wiki/Lithuanian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Lithuanian Soviet Socialist Republic").[[71]](#cite_note-VleListorija-75) In 1941 during the [June Uprising in Lithuania](/wiki/June_Uprising_in_Lithuania "June Uprising in Lithuania") it was attempted to restore independent Lithuania and the [Red Army](/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army") was expelled from its territory, however in a few days Lithuania was [occupied by Nazi Germany](/wiki/German_occupation_of_Lithuania_during_World_War_II "German occupation of Lithuania during World War II").[[71]](#cite_note-VleListorija-75) In 1944 Lithuania was [re-occupied by the Soviet Union](/wiki/Soviet_re-occupation_of_the_Baltic_states_(1944) "Soviet re-occupation of the Baltic states (1944)") and [Soviet political repressions](/wiki/Political_repression_in_the_Soviet_Union "Political repression in the Soviet Union") along with [Soviet deportations from Lithuania](/wiki/Soviet_deportations_from_Lithuania "Soviet deportations from Lithuania") resumed.[[71]](#cite_note-VleListorija-75) Thousands of [Lithuanian partisans](/wiki/Lithuanian_partisans "Lithuanian partisans") and their supporters attempted to militarily restore independent Lithuania, but their resistance was eventually suppressed in 1953 by the [Soviet authorities](/wiki/Chronology_of_Soviet_secret_police_agencies "Chronology of Soviet secret police agencies") and their [collaborators](/wiki/Extermination_battalion "Extermination battalion").[[71]](#cite_note-VleListorija-75) [Jonas Žemaitis](/wiki/Jonas_%C5%BDemaitis "Jonas Žemaitis"), the chairman of the [Union of Lithuanian Freedom Fighters](/wiki/Union_of_Lithuanian_Freedom_Fighters "Union of Lithuanian Freedom Fighters"), was captured and [executed](/wiki/Capital_punishment_in_the_Soviet_Union "Capital punishment in the Soviet Union") in 1954, his successor as chairman [Adolfas Ramanauskas](/wiki/Adolfas_Ramanauskas "Adolfas Ramanauskas") was brutally tortured and executed in 1957.[[72]](#cite_note-76)[[73]](#cite_note-77) Since the late 1980s [Sąjūdis](/wiki/S%C4%85j%C5%ABdis "Sąjūdis") movement sought for the restoration of independent Lithuania and in 1989 the [Baltic Way](/wiki/Baltic_Way "Baltic Way") was held.[[71]](#cite_note-VleListorija-75)

### 1990–present

Main article: [Act of the Re-Establishment of the State of Lithuania](/wiki/Act_of_the_Re-Establishment_of_the_State_of_Lithuania "Act of the Re-Establishment of the State of Lithuania")

See also: [Singing Revolution](/wiki/Singing_Revolution "Singing Revolution") and [Baltic Way](/wiki/Baltic_Way "Baltic Way")

On 11 March 1990, the [Supreme Council](/wiki/Supreme_Council_%E2%80%93_Reconstituent_Seimas "Supreme Council – Reconstituent Seimas") announced the [restoration of Lithuania's independence](/wiki/Act_of_the_Re-Establishment_of_the_State_of_Lithuania "Act of the Re-Establishment of the State of Lithuania").[[74]](#cite_note-Bell2002-78) After refusal to revoke the Act, [Soviet forces](/wiki/Soviet_Army "Soviet Army") stormed the [Seimas Palace](/wiki/Seimas_Palace "Seimas Palace") while Lithuanians defended the democratically elected Council. The Act, the first such declaration in the USSR, later was a model and inspiration to other [Soviet republics](/wiki/Soviet_republics "Soviet republics"), and strongly influenced the [dissolution of the Soviet Union](/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union "Dissolution of the Soviet Union").

On 11 March 1990, the [Supreme Council](/wiki/Supreme_Council_%E2%80%93_Reconstituent_Seimas "Supreme Council – Reconstituent Seimas") announced the restoration of Lithuania's independence. Lithuania became the first Soviet-occupied state to announce the restitution of independence.[[75]](#cite_note-:0-79) On 20 April 1990, the Soviets [imposed an economic blockade](/wiki/Soviet_economic_blockade_of_Lithuania "Soviet economic blockade of Lithuania") by ceasing to deliver supplies of raw materials to Lithuania.[[76]](#cite_note-80) Not only domestic industry, but also the population started feeling the lack of fuel, essential goods, and even hot water. Although the blockade lasted for 74 days, Lithuania did not renounce the declaration of independence.[[77]](#cite_note-LT1990-81)

Gradually, economic relations were restored. However, tensions peaked again in January 1991. Attempts were made to carry out a coup using the [Soviet Armed Forces](/wiki/Soviet_Armed_Forces "Soviet Armed Forces"), the Internal Army of the Ministry of Internal Affairs and the USSR Committee for State Security ([KGB](/wiki/KGB "KGB")). Because of the poor economic situation in Lithuania, the forces in Moscow thought the [coup d'état](/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "Coup d'état") would receive strong public support.[[78]](#cite_note-82) People flooded to Vilnius to defend the [Supreme Council of the Republic of Lithuania](/wiki/Supreme_Council_%E2%80%93_Reconstituent_Seimas "Supreme Council – Reconstituent Seimas") and independence. The coup ended with a few casualties and material loss. The [Soviet Army](/wiki/Soviet_Army "Soviet Army") killed 14 people and injured hundreds. A large part of the Lithuanian population participated in the [January Events](/wiki/January_Events "January Events").[[79]](#cite_note-bbc-83)[[80]](#cite_note-84)[[77]](#cite_note-LT1990-81) On 31 July 1991, Soviet paramilitaries killed 7 Lithuanian border guards on the Belarusian border in what became known as the [Medininkai Massacre](/wiki/Medininkai_Massacre "Medininkai Massacre").[[77]](#cite_note-LT1990-81) On 17 September 1991, Lithuania was admitted to the [United Nations](/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations").[[77]](#cite_note-LT1990-81)

On 25 October 1992, citizens voted in a referendum to adopt the current [constitution](/wiki/Constitution_of_Lithuania "Constitution of Lithuania").[[77]](#cite_note-LT1990-81) On 14 February 1993, during the direct general elections, [Algirdas Brazauskas](/wiki/Algirdas_Brazauskas "Algirdas Brazauskas") became the first president after the restoration of independence.[[77]](#cite_note-LT1990-81) On 31 August 1993 the last units of the former Soviet Army left Lithuania.[[81]](#cite_note-85)

On 31 May 2001, Lithuania joined the [World Trade Organization](/wiki/World_Trade_Organization "World Trade Organization") (WTO).[[82]](#cite_note-86) Since March 2004, Lithuania has been part of [NATO](/wiki/NATO "NATO").[[83]](#cite_note-87) On 1 May 2004, it became a full member of the [European Union](/wiki/European_Union "European Union"),[[84]](#cite_note-88) and a member of the [Schengen Agreement](/wiki/Schengen_Agreement "Schengen Agreement") in December 2007.[[85]](#cite_note-89) On 1 January 2015, [Lithuania joined](/wiki/Lithuania_and_the_euro "Lithuania and the euro") the [eurozone](/wiki/Eurozone "Eurozone") and adopted the European Union's single currency.[[86]](#cite_note-90) On 4 July 2018, Lithuania officially joined the [OECD](/wiki/OECD "OECD").[[87]](#cite_note-91) [Dalia Grybauskaitė](/wiki/Dalia_Grybauskait%C4%97 "Dalia Grybauskaitė") was the first female [President of Lithuania](/wiki/President_of_Lithuania "President of Lithuania") (2009–2019) and the first to be re-elected for a second consecutive term.[[88]](#cite_note-92) On 24 February 2022, Lithuania declared a [state of emergency](/wiki/State_of_emergency "State of emergency") in response to the 2022 [Russian invasion of Ukraine](/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "Russian invasion of Ukraine").[[89]](#cite_note-93) Together with seven other NATO member states, it invoked NATO [Article 4](/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty#Article_4 "North Atlantic Treaty") to hold consultations on security.[[90]](#cite_note-94) On 11–12 July 2023, the [2023 NATO summit](/wiki/2023_Vilnius_summit "2023 Vilnius summit") was held in Vilnius.[[91]](#cite_note-95)

Geography
---------

Main article: [Geography of Lithuania](/wiki/Geography_of_Lithuania "Geography of Lithuania")

Lithuania is located in the Baltic region of [Europe](/wiki/Europe "Europe")[[d]](#cite_note-location-28) and covers an area of 65,300 km2 (25,200 sq mi).[[92]](#cite_note-96) It lies between latitudes [53°](/wiki/53rd_parallel_north "53rd parallel north") and [57° N](/wiki/57th_parallel_north "57th parallel north"), and mostly between longitudes [21°](/wiki/21st_meridian_east "21st meridian east") and [27° E](/wiki/27th_meridian_east "27th meridian east") (part of the [Curonian Spit](/wiki/Curonian_Spit "Curonian Spit") lies west of 21°). It has around 99 kilometres (61.5 mi) of sandy coastline, only about 38 kilometres (24 mi) of which face the open [Baltic Sea](/wiki/Baltic_Sea "Baltic Sea"), less than the other two Baltic states. The rest of the coast is sheltered by the Curonian sand peninsula. Lithuania's major [warm-water port](/wiki/Warm-water_port "Warm-water port"), [Klaipėda](/wiki/Klaip%C4%97da "Klaipėda"), lies at the narrow mouth of the [Curonian Lagoon](/wiki/Curonian_Lagoon "Curonian Lagoon") (Lithuanian: *Kuršių marios*), a shallow lagoon extending south to [Kaliningrad](/wiki/Kaliningrad "Kaliningrad"). The country's main and largest river, the [Nemunas River](/wiki/Nemunas_River "Nemunas River"), and some of its tributaries carry international shipping.

Lithuania lies at the edge of the [North European Plain](/wiki/North_European_Plain "North European Plain"). Its landscape was smoothed by the glaciers of the [last ice age](/wiki/Last_glacial_period "Last glacial period"), and is a combination of moderate lowlands and highlands. Its highest point is [Aukštojas Hill](/wiki/Auk%C5%A1tojas_Hill "Aukštojas Hill") at 294 metres (965 ft) in the eastern part of the country. The terrain features [numerous lakes](/wiki/List_of_lakes_of_Lithuania "List of lakes of Lithuania") ([Lake Vištytis](/wiki/Lake_Vi%C5%A1tytis "Lake Vištytis"), for example) and wetlands, and a mixed forest zone covers over 33% of the country. [Drūkšiai](/wiki/Dr%C5%ABk%C5%A1iai "Drūkšiai") is the largest, [Tauragnas](/wiki/Tauragnas "Tauragnas") is the deepest and [Asveja](/wiki/Asveja "Asveja") is the longest lake in Lithuania.

After a re-estimation of the boundaries of the [continent](/wiki/Continent "Continent") of Europe in 1989, Jean-George Affholder, a scientist at the [Institut Géographique National](/wiki/Institut_g%C3%A9ographique_national_(France) "Institut géographique national (France)") (French National Geographic Institute), determined that the [geographic centre of Europe](/wiki/Geographic_centre_of_Europe "Geographic centre of Europe") was in Lithuania, at [54°54′N 25°19′E﻿ / ﻿54.900°N 25.317°E﻿ / 54.900; 25.317﻿ (Purnuškės (centre of gravity))](https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Lithuania&params=54_54_N_25_19_E_type:landmark&title=Purnu%C5%A1k%C4%97s+%28centre+of+gravity%29), 26 kilometres (16 mi) north of Lithuania's capital city of [Vilnius](/wiki/Vilnius "Vilnius").[[93]](#cite_note-97) Affholder accomplished this by calculating the [centre of gravity](/wiki/Centre_of_gravity "Centre of gravity") of the [geometrical figure](/wiki/Geography_of_Europe "Geography of Europe") of Europe.

### Climate

Main article: [Geography of Lithuania § Climate](/wiki/Geography_of_Lithuania#Climate "Geography of Lithuania")

Lithuania has a temperate climate with both [maritime](/wiki/Maritime_climate "Maritime climate") and [continental](/wiki/Continental_climate "Continental climate") influences. It is defined as [humid continental](/wiki/Humid_continental_climate "Humid continental climate") (Dfb) under the [Köppen climate classification](/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification "Köppen climate classification") (but is close to [oceanic](/wiki/Oceanic_climate "Oceanic climate") in a narrow coastal zone).

Average temperatures on the coast are −2.5 °C (27.5 °F) in January and 16 °C (61 °F) in July. In Vilnius, the average temperatures are −6 °C (21 °F) in January and 17 °C (63 °F) in July. During the summer, 20 °C (68 °F) is common during the day, while 14 °C (57 °F) is common at night; in the past, temperatures have reached as high as 30 or 35 °C (86 or 95 °F). Some winters can be very cold. −20 °C (−4 °F) occurs almost every winter. Winter extremes are −34 °C (−29 °F) in coastal areas and −43 °C (−45 °F) in the east of Lithuania.

The average annual precipitation is 800 mm (31.5 in) on the coast, 900 mm (35.4 in) in the Samogitia highlands, and 600 mm (23.6 in) in the eastern part of the country. Snow occurs every year, and it can snow from October to April. In some years, sleet can fall in September or May. The growing season lasts 202 days in the western part of the country and 169 days in the eastern part. Severe storms are rare in the eastern part of Lithuania but common in the coastal areas.

The longest records of measured temperature in the Baltic area cover about 250 years. The data show warm periods during the latter half of the 18th century, and that the 19th century was a relatively cool period. An early 20th-century warming culminated in the 1930s, followed by a smaller cooling that lasted until the 1960s. A warming trend has persisted since then.[[94]](#cite_note-98)

Lithuania experienced a drought in 2002, causing forest and [peat](/wiki/Peat "Peat") bog fires.[[95]](#cite_note-99)

### Biodiversity and conservation

Main articles: [Fauna of Lithuania](/wiki/Fauna_of_Lithuania "Fauna of Lithuania"), [Flora of Lithuania](/wiki/Flora_of_Lithuania "Flora of Lithuania"), and [Protected areas of Lithuania](/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Lithuania "Protected areas of Lithuania")

Lithuanian flatlands with lakes, swamps and forests. Lithuania has thousands of lakes.

Sand dunes of the [Curonian Spit](/wiki/Curonian_Spit "Curonian Spit") near [Nida](/wiki/Nida,_Lithuania "Nida, Lithuania"), which are the highest drifting sand dunes in Europe ([UNESCO World Heritage Site](/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site "UNESCO World Heritage Site"))[[96]](#cite_note-100)

After the restoration of Lithuania's independence in 1990, the *Aplinkos apsaugos įstatymas* (Environmental Protection Act) was adopted already in 1992. The law provided the foundations for regulating social relations in the field of environmental protection, established the basic rights and obligations of legal and natural persons in preserving the biodiversity inherent in Lithuania, ecological systems and the landscape.[[97]](#cite_note-101) Lithuania agreed to cut [carbon emissions](/wiki/Carbon_emissions "Carbon emissions") by at least 20% of 1990 levels by 2020 and by at least 40% by 2030, together with all European Union members. Also, by 2020 at least 20% (27% by 2030) of the country's total energy consumption should be from the [renewable energy](/wiki/Renewable_energy "Renewable energy") sources.[[98]](#cite_note-102) In 2016, Lithuania introduced especially effective [container deposit legislation](/wiki/Container_deposit_legislation "Container deposit legislation"), which resulted in collecting 92% of all packagings in 2017.[[99]](#cite_note-103)

Lithuania does not have high mountains and its landscape is dominated by blooming meadows, dense forests and fertile fields of cereals. However, it stands out by the abundance of [hillforts](/wiki/Hillfort "Hillfort"), which previously had castles where the ancient Lithuanians burned altars for pagan gods.[[100]](#cite_note-gamta-104) Lithuania is a particularly watered region with more than 3,000 lakes, mostly in the northeast. The country is also drained by numerous rivers, most notably the longest [Nemunas](/wiki/Nemunas "Nemunas").[[100]](#cite_note-gamta-104) Lithuania is home to two terrestrial ecoregions: [Central European mixed forests](/wiki/Central_European_mixed_forests "Central European mixed forests") and [Sarmatic mixed forests](/wiki/Sarmatic_mixed_forests "Sarmatic mixed forests").[[101]](#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-105)

Forest has long been one of the most important natural resources in Lithuania. Forests occupy one-third of the country's territory and timber-related industrial production accounts for almost 11% of industrial production in the country.[[102]](#cite_note-106) Lithuania has five [national parks](/wiki/List_of_national_parks_in_the_Baltics "List of national parks in the Baltics"),[[103]](#cite_note-107) 30 [regional parks](/wiki/List_of_regional_parks_of_Lithuania "List of regional parks of Lithuania"),[[104]](#cite_note-108) 402 [nature reserves](/wiki/Nature_reserve "Nature reserve"),[[105]](#cite_note-109) 6 [strict nature reserves](/wiki/Strict_nature_reserve "Strict nature reserve"),[[106]](#cite_note-110) 668 state-protected natural heritage objects.[[107]](#cite_note-111)

Lithuanian ecosystems include natural and semi-natural (forests, [bogs](/wiki/Bog "Bog"), wetlands and meadows), and anthropogenic (agrarian and urban) ecosystems. Among natural ecosystems, forests are particularly important to Lithuania, covering 33% of the country's territory. [Wetlands](/wiki/Wetland "Wetland") (raised bogs, [fens](/wiki/Fen "Fen"), transitional mires, etc.) cover 7.9% of the country, with 70% of wetlands having been lost due to drainage and peat extraction between 1960 and 1980. Changes in wetland plant communities resulted in the replacement of moss and grass communities by trees and shrubs, and fens not directly affected by land reclamation have become drier as a result of a drop in the water table. There are 29,000 rivers with a total length of 64,000 km in Lithuania, the [Nemunas River](/wiki/Nemunas_River "Nemunas River") basin occupying 74% of the territory of the country. Due to the construction of dams, approximately 70% of spawning sites of potential [catadromous](/wiki/Fish_migration "Fish migration") fish species have disappeared. In some cases, river and lake ecosystems continue to be impacted by anthropogenic [eutrophication](/wiki/Eutrophication "Eutrophication").[[110]](#cite_note-cbd-114)

Agricultural land comprises 54% of Lithuania's territory (roughly 70% of that is arable land and 30% meadows and pastures), approximately 400,000 ha of agricultural land is not farmed, and acts as an ecological niche for weeds and invasive plant species. Habitat deterioration is occurring in regions with very productive and expensive lands as crop areas are expanded. Currently, 18.9% of all plant species, including 1.87% of all known fungi species and 31% of all known species of lichens, are listed in the [Lithuanian Red Data Book](/wiki/List_of_extinct_and_endangered_species_of_Lithuania "List of extinct and endangered species of Lithuania"). The list also contains 8% of all fish species.[[110]](#cite_note-cbd-114)

The wildlife populations have rebounded as the hunting became more restricted and urbanization allowed replanting forests (forests already tripled in size since their lows). Currently, Lithuania has approximately 250,000 larger wild animals or 5 per each square kilometre. The most prolific large wild animal in every part of Lithuania is the [roe deer](/wiki/Roe_deer "Roe deer"), with 120,000 of them. They are followed by [boars](/wiki/Boar "Boar") (55,000). Other ungulates are the [deer](/wiki/Deer "Deer") (~22,000), [fallow-deer](/wiki/Fallow-deer "Fallow-deer") (~21,000) and the largest one: [moose](/wiki/Moose "Moose") (~7,000). Among the Lithuanian predators, [foxes](/wiki/Fox "Fox") are the most common (~27,000). [Wolves](/wiki/Wolve "Wolve") are, however, more ingrained into the mythology as there are just 800 in Lithuania. Even rarer are the [lynxes](/wiki/Lynx "Lynx") (~200). The large animals mentioned above exclude the [rabbit](/wiki/Rabbit "Rabbit"), ~200,000 of which may live in the Lithuanian forests.[[111]](#cite_note-115)

Government and politics
-----------------------

Main article: [Politics of Lithuania](/wiki/Politics_of_Lithuania "Politics of Lithuania")

### Government

Since Lithuania declared the restoration of its independence on 11 March 1990, it has maintained strong democratic traditions. It held its first independent general elections on 25 October 1992, in which 56.75% of voters supported the [new constitution](/wiki/Constitution_of_Lithuania "Constitution of Lithuania").[[112]](#cite_note-referenda-116) There were intense debates concerning the constitution, particularly the role of the president. A [separate referendum](/wiki/1992_Lithuanian_presidency_referendum "1992 Lithuanian presidency referendum") was held on 23 May 1992 to gauge public opinion on the matter, and 41% of voters supported the restoration of the [President of Lithuania](/wiki/President_of_Lithuania "President of Lithuania").[[112]](#cite_note-referenda-116) Through compromise, a [semi-presidential system](/wiki/Semi-presidential_system "Semi-presidential system") was agreed on.[[4]](#cite_note-Lina-4)

[Gitanas Nausėda](/wiki/Gitanas_Naus%C4%97da "Gitanas Nausėda"),  
[President](/wiki/President_of_Lithuania "President of Lithuania") since 2019

[Gintautas Paluckas](/wiki/Gintautas_Paluckas "Gintautas Paluckas"),  
[Prime Minister](/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Lithuania "Prime Minister of Lithuania") since 2024

[Saulius Skvernelis](/wiki/Saulius_Skvernelis "Saulius Skvernelis"),  
[Speaker of the Seimas](/wiki/Speaker_of_the_Seimas "Speaker of the Seimas") since 2024

The Lithuanian [head of state](/wiki/Head_of_state "Head of state") is the president, directly elected for a five-year term and serving a maximum of two terms. The president oversees foreign affairs and national security, and is the [commander-in-chief](/wiki/Commander-in-chief "Commander-in-chief") of the military.[[113]](#cite_note-lrpf-117) The president also appoints the [prime minister](/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Lithuania "Prime Minister of Lithuania") and, on the latter's nomination, the rest of the cabinet, as well as a number of other top civil servants and the judges for all courts except the Constitutional Court.[[113]](#cite_note-lrpf-117) The current Lithuanian head of state, [Gitanas Nausėda](/wiki/Gitanas_Naus%C4%97da "Gitanas Nausėda") was [elected on 26 May 2019](/wiki/2019_Lithuanian_presidential_election "2019 Lithuanian presidential election") by winning in all the [municipalities of Lithuania](/wiki/Municipalities_of_Lithuania "Municipalities of Lithuania") in the second election round.[[114]](#cite_note-president2019-118) He was re-elected in 2024, winning more than 74% of the run-off votes.[[115]](#cite_note-119)

The judges of the [Constitutional Court](/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Lithuania "Constitutional Court of Lithuania") (*Konstitucinis Teismas*) serve nine-year terms. The court is renewed by a third every three years. The judges are appointed by the Seimas, on the nomination by the President, Chairman of the Seimas, and the Chairman of the Supreme Court. The [unicameral](/wiki/Unicameral "Unicameral") Lithuanian parliament, the [Seimas](/wiki/Seimas "Seimas"), has 141 members elected to four-year terms - 71 in single-member constituencies, and the others in a nationwide vote by [proportional representation](/wiki/Proportional_representation "Proportional representation"). A party must receive at least 5% of the national vote to be eligible for any of the 70 national seats in the Seimas.[[116]](#cite_note-Seimas-120)

### Political parties and elections

Main article: [Elections in Lithuania](/wiki/Elections_in_Lithuania "Elections in Lithuania")

Lithuania was one of the first countries in the world to [grant women a right to vote](/wiki/Women%27s_suffrage "Women's suffrage") in the elections. Lithuanian women were allowed to vote by the [1918 Constitution of Lithuania](/wiki/Constitution_of_Lithuania#Interwar_constitutions "Constitution of Lithuania") and used their newly granted right for the first time in 1919. By doing so, Lithuania allowed it earlier than such democratic countries as the [United States](/wiki/United_States "United States") (1920), [France](/wiki/France "France") (1945), [Greece](/wiki/Feminism_in_Greece "Feminism in Greece") (1952), [Switzerland](/wiki/Switzerland "Switzerland") (1971).[[117]](#cite_note-121)

Lithuania exhibits a fragmented multi-party system,[[118]](#cite_note-122) with a number of small parties in which coalition governments are common. Ordinary elections to the [Seimas](/wiki/Seimas "Seimas") take place on the second Sunday of October every four years.[[116]](#cite_note-Seimas-120) To be eligible for election, candidates must be at least 21 years old on the election day, not under allegiance to a foreign state and permanently reside in Lithuania.[[119]](#cite_note-123) Persons serving or due to serve a sentence imposed by the court 65 days before the election are not eligible. Also, judges, citizens performing military service, and servicemen of professional military service and officials of statutory institutions and establishments may not stand for election.[[120]](#cite_note-124) [Social Democratic Party of Lithuania](/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Lithuania "Social Democratic Party of Lithuania") won the [2024 Lithuanian parliamentary elections](/wiki/2024_Lithuanian_parliamentary_election "2024 Lithuanian parliamentary election") and gained 52 of 141 seats in the parliament.[[121]](#cite_note-125) In November 2024, [Gintautas Paluckas](/wiki/Gintautas_Paluckas "Gintautas Paluckas") was confirmed as the prime minister after the Social Democrats reached a coalition agreement with [Union of Democrats "For Lithuania"](/wiki/Union_of_Democrats_%22For_Lithuania%22 "Union of Democrats \"For Lithuania\"") and [Dawn of Nemunas](/wiki/Dawn_of_Nemunas "Dawn of Nemunas").[[122]](#cite_note-126)

The [President of Lithuania](/wiki/President_of_Lithuania "President of Lithuania") is the head of state of the country, elected to a five-year term in a majority vote. Elections take place on the last Sunday no more than two months before the end of current presidential term.[[123]](#cite_note-Constitution-127) To be eligible for election, candidates must be at least 40 years old on the election day and reside in Lithuania for at least three years, in addition to satisfying the eligibility criteria for a member of the parliament. Same President may serve for not more than two terms.[[124]](#cite_note-128) [Gitanas Nausėda](/wiki/Gitanas_Naus%C4%97da "Gitanas Nausėda") was elected as an independent candidate in [2019](/wiki/2019_Lithuanian_presidential_election "2019 Lithuanian presidential election") and re-elected in [2024](/wiki/2024_Lithuanian_presidential_election "2024 Lithuanian presidential election").[[125]](#cite_note-129)

Each municipality in Lithuania is governed by a [municipal council](/wiki/Municipal_council "Municipal council") and a [mayor](/wiki/Mayor "Mayor"), who is a member of the municipal council. The number of members, elected on a four-year term, in each municipal council depends on the size of the municipality and varies from 15 (in municipalities with fewer than 5,000 residents) to 51 (in municipalities with more than 500,000 residents). 1,498 municipal council members were elected in 2023. Members of the council, with the exception of the mayor, are elected using proportional representation. Starting with 2015, the mayor is elected directly by the majority of residents of the municipality.[[126]](#cite_note-130) [Social Democratic Party of Lithuania](/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Lithuania "Social Democratic Party of Lithuania") won the most positions in the 2023 elections (358 municipal council seats and 17 mayors).[[127]](#cite_note-131)

As of 2024, the number of seats in the [European Parliament](/wiki/European_Parliament "European Parliament") allocated to Lithuania was 11.[[128]](#cite_note-132) Ordinary elections take place on a Sunday on the same day as in other EU countries. The vote is open to all citizens of Lithuania, as well as citizens of other EU countries that permanently reside in Lithuania, who are at least 18 years old on the election day. To be eligible for election, candidates must be at least 21 years old on the election day, a citizen of Lithuania or a citizen of another EU country permanently residing in Lithuania. Candidates are not allowed to stand for election in more than one country. Persons serving or due to serve a sentence imposed by the court 65 days before the election are not eligible. Also, judges, citizens performing military service, and servicemen of professional military service and officials of statutory institutions and establishments may not stand for election.[[129]](#cite_note-133) Eight political parties gained seats in the [2024 elections](/wiki/2024_European_Parliament_election_in_Lithuania "2024 European Parliament election in Lithuania").[[130]](#cite_note-134)

### Law and law enforcement

Main article: [Law of Lithuania](/wiki/Law_of_Lithuania "Law of Lithuania")

The first attempt to [codify](/wiki/Codification_(law) "Codification (law)") the Lithuanian laws was in 1468 when the [Casimir's Code](/wiki/Casimir%27s_Code "Casimir's Code") was compiled and adopted by Grand Duke [Casimir IV Jagiellon](/wiki/Casimir_IV_Jagiellon "Casimir IV Jagiellon").[[131]](#cite_note-LawVle-135) In the 16th century three editions of the [Statutes of Lithuania](/wiki/Statutes_of_Lithuania "Statutes of Lithuania") were created with the First Statute being adopted in 1529, the Second Statute in 1566, and the Third Statute in 1588.[[131]](#cite_note-LawVle-135) On 3 May 1791, the Europe's first and the world's second [Constitution](/wiki/Constitution_of_3_May_1791 "Constitution of 3 May 1791") was adopted by the [Great Sejm](/wiki/Great_Sejm "Great Sejm").[[132]](#cite_note-136) The Third Statute was partly in force in the territory of Lithuania even until 1840, despite the [Third Partition of the Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth](/wiki/Partitions_of_Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth "Partitions of Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth") in 1795.[[131]](#cite_note-LawVle-135)

In 1934–1935, Lithuania held the [first mass trial of the Nazis in Europe](/wiki/Trial_of_Neumann_and_Sass "Trial of Neumann and Sass"), the [convicted](/wiki/Conviction "Conviction") were sentenced to imprisonment in a [heavy labor prison](/wiki/Penal_labour "Penal labour") and [capital punishments](/wiki/Capital_punishment "Capital punishment").[[133]](#cite_note-137)

After regaining of independence in 1990, the largely modified Soviet legal codes were in force for about a decade. The current [Constitution of Lithuania](/wiki/Constitution_of_Lithuania "Constitution of Lithuania") was adopted on 25 October 1992.[[134]](#cite_note-138) In 2001, the [Civil Code of Lithuania](/wiki/Civil_Code_of_Lithuania "Civil Code of Lithuania") was passed in [Seimas](/wiki/Seimas "Seimas"). It was succeeded by the [Criminal Code](/wiki/Criminal_Code "Criminal Code") and [Criminal Procedure](/wiki/Criminal_Procedure "Criminal Procedure") Code in 2003. The approach to the [criminal law](/wiki/Criminal_law "Criminal law") is [inquisitorial](/wiki/Inquisitorial "Inquisitorial"), as opposed to [adversarial](/wiki/Adversarial_system "Adversarial system"); it is generally characterised by an insistence on formality and rationalisation, as opposed to practicality and informality. Normative legal act enters into force on the next day after its publication in the *Teisės aktų registras*, unless it has a later entry into force date.[[135]](#cite_note-139)

The [European Union law](/wiki/European_Union_law "European Union law") is an integral part of the Lithuanian legal system since 1 May 2004.[[136]](#cite_note-140)

Lithuania, after breaking away from the Soviet Union, had a difficult crime situation, however, the Lithuanian law enforcement agencies fought crime over the years, making Lithuania a reasonably safe country.[[137]](#cite_note-141) Crime in Lithuania has been declining rapidly.[[138]](#cite_note-142) Law enforcement in Lithuania is primarily the responsibility of local *Lietuvos policija* (Lithuanian Police) commissariats. They are supplemented by the *Lietuvos policijos antiteroristinių operacijų rinktinė Aras* (Anti-Terrorist Operations Team of the Lithuanian Police *Aras*), *Lietuvos kriminalinės policijos biuras* (Lithuanian Criminal Police Bureau), *Lietuvos policijos kriminalistinių tyrimų centras* (Lithuanian Police Forensic Research Center) and *Lietuvos kelių policijos tarnyba* (Lithuanian Road Police Service).[[139]](#cite_note-143)

In 2017, there were 63,846 crimes registered in Lithuania. Of these, thefts comprised a large part with 19,630 cases (13.2% less than in 2016). While 2,835 crimes were serious and very serious (crimes that may lead to more than six years imprisonment), which is 14.5% less than in 2016. In total, 129 homicides or attempted homicide occurred (19.9% less than in 2016), while serious bodily harm was registered 178 times (17.6% less than in 2016). Another problematic crime [contraband](/wiki/Contraband "Contraband") cases also decreased by 27.2% from 2016 numbers. Meanwhile, crimes in electronic data and information technology security fields noticeably increased by 26.6%.[[140]](#cite_note-144) In the 2013 Special Eurobarometer, 29% of Lithuanians said that corruption affects their daily lives (EU average 26%). Moreover, 95% of Lithuanians regarded corruption as widespread in their country (EU average 76%), and 88% agreed that bribery and the use of connections is often the easiest way of obtaining certain public services (EU average 73%).[[141]](#cite_note-145) Though, according to local branch of Transparency International, corruption levels have been decreasing over the past decade.[[142]](#cite_note-146)

[Capital punishment in Lithuania](/wiki/Capital_punishment_in_Lithuania "Capital punishment in Lithuania") was suspended in 1996 and eliminated in 1998.[[143]](#cite_note-147) Lithuania has the highest number of prison inmates in the EU. According to scientist Gintautas Sakalauskas, this is not because of a high criminality rate in the country, but due to Lithuania's high repression level and the lack of trust of the convicted, who are frequently sentenced to imprisonment.[[144]](#cite_note-148)

### Administrative divisions

Main article: [Administrative divisions of Lithuania](/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Lithuania "Administrative divisions of Lithuania")

See also: [Counties of Lithuania](/wiki/Counties_of_Lithuania "Counties of Lithuania"), [Municipalities of Lithuania](/wiki/Municipalities_of_Lithuania "Municipalities of Lithuania"), [Elderships of Lithuania](/wiki/Elderships_of_Lithuania "Elderships of Lithuania"), and [Cultural regions of Lithuania](/wiki/Cultural_regions_of_Lithuania "Cultural regions of Lithuania")

[Alytus County](/wiki/Alytus_County "Alytus County")

[Kaunas County](/wiki/Kaunas_County "Kaunas County")

[Klaipėda  
County](/wiki/Klaip%C4%97da_County "Klaipėda County")

[Marijampolė  
County](/wiki/Marijampol%C4%97_County "Marijampolė County")

[Panevėžys County](/wiki/Panev%C4%97%C5%BEys_County "Panevėžys County")

[Šiauliai County](/wiki/%C5%A0iauliai_County "Šiauliai County")

[Tauragė County](/wiki/Taurag%C4%97_County "Tauragė County")

[Telšiai County](/wiki/Tel%C5%A1iai_County "Telšiai County")

[Utena County](/wiki/Utena_County "Utena County")

[Vilnius County](/wiki/Vilnius_County "Vilnius County")

*[Baltic Sea](/wiki/Baltic_Sea "Baltic Sea")*

*[Latvia](/wiki/Latvia "Latvia")*

*[Belarus](/wiki/Belarus "Belarus")*

*[Poland](/wiki/Poland "Poland")*

*[Russia](/wiki/Russia "Russia")*

The current system of administrative division was established in 1994 and modified in 2000 to meet the requirements of the European Union. The country's [10 counties](/wiki/Counties_of_Lithuania "Counties of Lithuania") (Lithuanian: singular – *apskritis*, plural – *apskritys*) are subdivided into [60 municipalities](/wiki/Municipalities_of_Lithuania "Municipalities of Lithuania") (Lithuanian: singular – *savivaldybė*, plural – *savivaldybės*), and further divided into 546 [elderships](/wiki/Elderships_of_Lithuania "Elderships of Lithuania") (Lithuanian: singular – *seniūnija*, plural – *seniūnijos*). There are also 5 distinct [cultural regions](/wiki/Cultural_regions_of_Lithuania "Cultural regions of Lithuania") in Lithuania – [Dzūkija](/wiki/Dz%C5%ABkija "Dzūkija"), [Aukštaitija](/wiki/Auk%C5%A1taitija "Aukštaitija"), [Suvalkija](/wiki/Suvalkija "Suvalkija"), [Samogitia](/wiki/Samogitia "Samogitia") and [Lithuania Minor](/wiki/Lithuania_Minor "Lithuania Minor"), which are recognized by the state.

Municipalities have been the most important unit of administration in Lithuania since the system of [county governorship](/wiki/County_governor_(Lithuania) "County governor (Lithuania)") (*apskrities viršininkas*) was dissolved in 2010.[[145]](#cite_note-county-149) Some municipalities are historically called "district municipalities" (often shortened to "district"), while others are called "city municipalities" (sometimes shortened to "city"). Each has its own elected government. The election of municipality councils originally occurred every three years, but now takes place every four years. The council appoints [elders](/wiki/Elder_(administrative_title) "Elder (administrative title)") to govern the elderships. Mayors have been directly elected since 2015; prior to that, they were appointed by the council.[[146]](#cite_note-150)

Elderships, numbering over 500, are the smallest administrative units and do not play a role in national politics. They provide necessary local public services—for example, registering births and deaths in rural areas. They are most active in the social sector, identifying needy individuals or families and organizing and distributing welfare and other forms of relief.[[147]](#cite_note-elderates-151) Some citizens feel that elderships have no real power and receive too little attention, and that they could otherwise become a source of local initiative for addressing rural problems.[[148]](#cite_note-152)

| [Marijampolė County](/wiki/Marijampol%C4%97_County "Marijampolė County") | 4,463 | 135,891 | 2.0 | 14,400 |
| [Panevėžys County](/wiki/Panev%C4%97%C5%BEys_County "Panevėžys County") | 7,881 | 211,652 | 3.6 | 17,100 |
