### Health

Main article: [Health in Lithuania](/wiki/Health_in_Lithuania "Health in Lithuania")

Lithuania provides free state-funded healthcare to all citizens and registered long-term residents.[[330]](#cite_note-334) It co-exists with a significant private healthcare sector. In 2003–2012, the network of hospitals was restructured, as part of wider healthcare service reforms. It started in 2003–2005 with the expansion of ambulatory services and primary care.[[331]](#cite_note-335)
In 2016, Lithuania ranked 27th in Europe in the [Euro health consumer index](/wiki/Euro_health_consumer_index "Euro health consumer index"), a ranking of European healthcare systems based on waiting time, results and other indicators. Lithuania ranked 19th in the 2024 edition of the [World Happiness Report](/wiki/World_Happiness_Report "World Happiness Report").[[332]](#cite_note-:1-336)

As of 2023[[update]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lithuania&action=edit), Lithuanian [life expectancy](/wiki/Life_expectancy "Life expectancy") at birth was 76.0 (70.6 years for males and 81.6 for females)[[333]](#cite_note-337) and the [infant mortality](/wiki/Infant_mortality "Infant mortality") rate was 2.99 per 1,000 births.[[334]](#cite_note-338) The annual population growth rate increased by 0.3% in 2007. Lithuania has seen a dramatic rise in suicides in the 1990s.[[335]](#cite_note-who-suicide-data-339) The suicide rate has been constantly decreasing since, but it still remains the highest in the EU and one of the highest in the [OECD](/wiki/OECD "OECD"). The suicide rate as of 2019 is 20.2 per 100,000 people.[[335]](#cite_note-who-suicide-data-339) [Suicide in Lithuania](/wiki/Suicide_in_Lithuania "Suicide in Lithuania") has been a subject of research, but the main reasons behind the high rate are thought[*[who?](/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions "Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch")*] to be both psychological and economic, including: social transformations and economic recessions, alcoholism, lack of tolerance in the society and bullying.[[336]](#cite_note-lrt-suicide-reasons-340)

By 2000, the vast majority of Lithuanian health care institutions were non-profit-making enterprises and a private sector developed, providing mostly outpatient services which are paid for out-of-pocket. The [Ministry of Health](/wiki/Ministry_of_Health_(Lithuania) "Ministry of Health (Lithuania)") also runs a few health care facilities and is involved in the running of the two major Lithuanian teaching hospitals. It is responsible for the State Public Health Centre which manages the public health network including ten county public health centres with their local branches. The ten [counties](/wiki/Counties_of_Lithuania "Counties of Lithuania") run county hospitals and specialised health care facilities.[[337]](#cite_note-341)

There is [Compulsory Health Insurance](/wiki/Taxation_in_Lithuania#Social_security_contributions "Taxation in Lithuania") for the Lithuanian residents. There are 5 Territorial Health Insurance Funds, covering Vilnius, Kaunas, Klaipėda, Šiauliai and Panevėžys. Contributions for people who are economically active are 9% of income.[[338]](#cite_note-342)

Emergency medical services are provided free of charge to all residents. Access to the secondary and tertiary care, such as hospital treatment, is normally via referral by a [general practitioner](/wiki/General_practitioner "General practitioner").[[339]](#cite_note-343) Lithuania also has one of the lowest [health care](/wiki/Health_care "Health care") prices in Europe.[[340]](#cite_note-344)

### Religion

Main article: [Religion in Lithuania](/wiki/Religion_in_Lithuania "Religion in Lithuania")

See also: [Lithuanian mythology](/wiki/Lithuanian_mythology "Lithuanian mythology")

According to the 2021 census, 74.2% of residents of Lithuania were Catholics.[[3]](#cite_note-religion-stats-3) Catholicism has been the main religion since the official [Christianisation of Lithuania](/wiki/Christianisation_of_Lithuania "Christianisation of Lithuania") in 1387. The Catholic Church was persecuted by the Russian Empire as part of the [Russification](/wiki/Russification "Russification") policies and by the Soviet Union as part of the overall [anti-religious campaigns](/wiki/Religion_in_the_Soviet_Union "Religion in the Soviet Union"). During the Soviet era, some priests actively led the resistance against the Communist regime, as symbolised by the [Hill of Crosses](/wiki/Hill_of_Crosses "Hill of Crosses") and exemplified by *[The Chronicle of the Catholic Church in Lithuania](/wiki/The_Chronicle_of_the_Catholic_Church_in_Lithuania "The Chronicle of the Catholic Church in Lithuania")*.

3.7% of the population are [Eastern Orthodox](/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church "Eastern Orthodox Church"), mainly among the Russian minority.[[3]](#cite_note-religion-stats-3) The community of [Old Believers](/wiki/Old_Believers "Old Believers") (0.6% of population) dates back to the 1660s.

[Protestants](/wiki/Protestants "Protestants") are 0.8%, of which 0.6% are [Lutheran](/wiki/Lutheranism "Lutheranism") and 0.2% are [Reformed](/wiki/Lithuanian_Evangelical_Reformed_Church "Lithuanian Evangelical Reformed Church"). The [Reformation](/wiki/Reformation "Reformation") did not impact Lithuania to a great extent as seen in [East Prussia](/wiki/East_Prussia "East Prussia"), [Estonia](/wiki/Estonia "Estonia"), or [Latvia](/wiki/Latvia "Latvia"). Before World War II, according to Losch (1932), the Lutherans were 3.3% of the total population.[[341]](#cite_note-lmaleidykla.lt-345) They were mainly [Germans](/wiki/Germans "Germans") and [Prussian Lithuanians](/wiki/Prussian_Lithuanians "Prussian Lithuanians") in the [Klaipėda Region](/wiki/Klaip%C4%97da_Region "Klaipėda Region") (Memel territory). This population [fled or was expelled after the war](/wiki/Flight_and_expulsion_of_Germans "Flight and expulsion of Germans"), and Protestantism is now mainly represented by ethnic Lithuanians throughout the northern and western parts of the country, as well as in large urban areas. Newly arriving [evangelical churches](/wiki/Evangelicalism "Evangelicalism") have established missions in Lithuania since 1990.[[342]](#cite_note-346)

Hinduism is a minority religion and a fairly recent development in Lithuania. Hinduism is spread in Lithuania by Hindu organizations: [ISKCON](/wiki/ISKCON "ISKCON"), [Sathya Sai Baba](/wiki/Sathya_Sai_Baba "Sathya Sai Baba"), [Brahma Kumaris](/wiki/Brahma_Kumaris "Brahma Kumaris") and [Osho Rajneesh](/wiki/Osho_Rajneesh "Osho Rajneesh"). [ISKCON](/wiki/ISKCON "ISKCON") (Lithuanian: Krišnos sąmonės judėjimas) is the largest and the oldest movement as the first Krishna followers date to 1979.[[343]](#cite_note-347) It has three centres in Lithuania: in [Vilnius](/wiki/Vilnius "Vilnius"), [Klaipėda](/wiki/Klaip%C4%97da "Klaipėda") and [Kaunas](/wiki/Kaunas "Kaunas"). [Brahma Kumaris](/wiki/Brahma_Kumaris "Brahma Kumaris") maintains the Centre Brahma Kumaris in [Antakalnis](/wiki/Antakalnis "Antakalnis"), Vilnius.

The historical communities of [Lipka Tatars](/wiki/Lipka_Tatars "Lipka Tatars") maintain [Islam](/wiki/Islam_in_Lithuania "Islam in Lithuania") as their religion. Lithuania was historically home to a significant [Jewish community](/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Lithuania "History of the Jews in Lithuania") and was an important centre of Jewish scholarship and culture from the 18th century until the eve of World War II. Of the approximately 220,000 Jews who lived in Lithuania in June 1941, almost all were killed during [the Holocaust](/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Lithuania "The Holocaust in Lithuania").[[344]](#cite_note-Bubnys_vanished219-348)[[345]](#cite_note-349) The Lithuanian Jewish community numbered about 4,000 at the end of 2009.[[346]](#cite_note-Stats-350)

[Romuva](/wiki/Romuva_(religion) "Romuva (religion)"), the [neopagan](/wiki/Neopagan "Neopagan") revival of the [ancient religious practices](/wiki/Lithuanian_mythology "Lithuanian mythology"), has gained popularity over the years. Romuva claims to continue living pagan traditions, which survived in folklore and customs.[[347]](#cite_note-351)[[348]](#cite_note-352)[[349]](#cite_note-353) Romuva is a [polytheistic](/wiki/Polytheism "Polytheism") pagan faith, which asserts the sanctity of nature and has elements of [ancestor worship](/wiki/Ancestor_worship "Ancestor worship").[[350]](#cite_note-354) According to the [2001 census](/wiki/Lithuanian_census_of_2001 "Lithuanian census of 2001"), there were 1,270 people of Baltic faith in Lithuania.[[351]](#cite_note-355) That number jumped to 5,118 in the 2011 census.[[352]](#cite_note-osp.stat.gov.lt-356)

### Education

Main article: [Education in Lithuania](/wiki/Education_in_Lithuania "Education in Lithuania")

See also: [List of universities and colleges in Lithuania](/wiki/List_of_universities_and_colleges_in_Lithuania "List of universities and colleges in Lithuania")

The [Constitution of Lithuania](/wiki/Constitution_of_Lithuania "Constitution of Lithuania") mandates ten-year education ending at age 16 and guarantees a free public higher education for students deemed 'good'.[[354]](#cite_note-358) The [Ministry of Education and Science of the Republic of Lithuania](/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_and_Science_(Lithuania) "Ministry of Education and Science (Lithuania)") proposes national educational policies and goals that are then voted for in the Seimas. Laws govern long-term educational strategy along with general laws on standards for higher education, vocational training, law and science, adult education, and special education.[[355]](#cite_note-edu1-359) 5.4% of GDP or 15.4% of total public expenditure was spent for education in 2016.[[356]](#cite_note-edumonitor-360)

According to the [World Bank](/wiki/World_Bank "World Bank"), the literacy rate among Lithuanians aged 15 years and older is 100%.[[357]](#cite_note-361) School attendance rates are above the EU average and school leave is less common than in the EU. According to [Eurostat](/wiki/Eurostat "Eurostat") Lithuania leads among other countries of the [European Union](/wiki/European_Union "European Union") in people with secondary education (93.3%).[[358]](#cite_note-362) Based on OECD data, Lithuania is among the top 5 countries in the world in postsecondary (tertiary) education attainment.[[359]](#cite_note-363) As of 2016[[update]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lithuania&action=edit), 54.9% of the population aged 25 to 34, and 30.7% of the population aged 55 to 64 had completed tertiary education.[[360]](#cite_note-364) The share of tertiary-educated 25–64-year-olds in STEM ([Science, technology, engineering, and mathematics](/wiki/Science,_technology,_engineering,_and_mathematics "Science, technology, engineering, and mathematics")) fields in Lithuania were above the OECD average (29% and 26% respectively), similarly to business, administration and law (25% and 23% respectively).[[361]](#cite_note-365)

Modern Lithuanian education system has multiple structural problems. Insufficient funding, quality issues, and decreasing student population are the most prevalent. Lithuanian teacher salaries below EU average, despite significant increases since 2011.[[362]](#cite_note-366) Low teacher salaries was the primary reason behind national teacher strikes in 2014,[[363]](#cite_note-367) 2015,[[364]](#cite_note-368) and 2016.[[365]](#cite_note-369)[[366]](#cite_note-370) Salaries in the higher education sector are also low. Many Lithuanian professors have a second job to supplement their income.[[367]](#cite_note-371) PISA report from 2022 found that Lithuanian results in math, science and reading were around OECD average, after trailing the OECD average in earlier reports in 2010 and 2015, although the relative improvement was primarily driven by the decrease in performance in the other OECD countries as a result of COVID 19 pandemic.[[368]](#cite_note-372)[[369]](#cite_note-373)[[370]](#cite_note-374) The population ages 6 to 19 has decreased by 36% between 2005 and 2015. As a result, the student-teacher ratio is decreasing and expenditure per student is increasing, but schools, particularly in rural areas, are forced into reorganizations and consolidations.[[356]](#cite_note-edumonitor-360) As with other Baltic nations, in particular [Latvia](/wiki/Latvia "Latvia"), the large volume of higher education graduates within the country, coupled with the high rate of spoken second languages is contributing to an education [brain drain](/wiki/Brain_drain "Brain drain").

As of 2008[[update]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lithuania&action=edit), there were 15 public and 6 private universities as well as 16 public and 11 private colleges in Lithuania (see: [List of universities in Lithuania](/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Lithuania "List of universities in Lithuania")).[[371]](#cite_note-375) [Vilnius University](/wiki/Vilnius_University "Vilnius University") is one of the [oldest universities in Northern Europe](/wiki/List_of_oldest_universities_in_continuous_operation "List of oldest universities in continuous operation") and the largest university in Lithuania. [Kaunas University of Technology](/wiki/Kaunas_University_of_Technology "Kaunas University of Technology") is the largest technical university in the Baltic States and the second largest university in Lithuania. In an attempt to reduce costs[[372]](#cite_note-376) and adapt to sharply decreasing number of high-school students,[[373]](#cite_note-377) Lithuanian parliament decided to reduce the number of universities in Lithuania.[[374]](#cite_note-378)[[375]](#cite_note-379) In early 2018, [Lithuanian University of Educational Sciences](/wiki/Lithuanian_University_of_Educational_Sciences "Lithuanian University of Educational Sciences") and [Aleksandras Stulginskis University](/wiki/Aleksandras_Stulginskis_University "Aleksandras Stulginskis University") were merged into [Vytautas Magnus University](/wiki/Vytautas_Magnus_University "Vytautas Magnus University").[[376]](#cite_note-380)

Culture
-------

Main article: [Culture of Lithuania](/wiki/Culture_of_Lithuania "Culture of Lithuania")

See also: [List of Lithuanians](/wiki/List_of_Lithuanians "List of Lithuanians")

### Lithuanian language

Main article: [Lithuanian language](/wiki/Lithuanian_language "Lithuanian language")

A priest, lexicographer [Konstantinas Sirvydas](/wiki/Konstantinas_Sirvydas "Konstantinas Sirvydas") – cherisher of Lithuanian language in the 17th century

[Jonas Jablonskis](/wiki/Jonas_Jablonskis "Jonas Jablonskis") is the father of standard Lithuanian language.

The [Lithuanian language](/wiki/Lithuanian_language "Lithuanian language") (*lietuvių kalba*) is the official state language of Lithuania and is recognized as one of the [official languages](/wiki/Official_language "Official language") of the [European Union](/wiki/European_Union "European Union"). There are about 2.96 million native Lithuanian speakers in Lithuania and about 0.2 million abroad.

Lithuanian is a [Baltic language](/wiki/Baltic_languages "Baltic languages"), closely related to [Latvian](/wiki/Latvian_language "Latvian language"), although they are not [mutually intelligible](/wiki/Mutual_intelligibility "Mutual intelligibility"). It is written in an adapted version of the [Roman script](/wiki/Latin_alphabet "Latin alphabet"). Lithuanian is believed to be the [linguistically most conservative](/wiki/Conservative_(language) "Conservative (language)") living [Indo-European tongue](/wiki/Indo-European_languages "Indo-European languages"), retaining many features of [Proto Indo-European](/wiki/Proto_Indo-European_language "Proto Indo-European language").[[377]](#cite_note-zinkevicius-381) Lithuanian language studies are important for [comparative linguistics](/wiki/Comparative_linguistics "Comparative linguistics") and for reconstruction of [Proto-Indo-European language](/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language "Proto-Indo-European language").[[378]](#cite_note-382) Lithuanian was studied by linguists such as [Franz Bopp](/wiki/Franz_Bopp "Franz Bopp"), [August Schleicher](/wiki/August_Schleicher "August Schleicher"), [Adalbert Bezzenberger](/wiki/Adalbert_Bezzenberger "Adalbert Bezzenberger"), [Louis Hjelmslev](/wiki/Louis_Hjelmslev "Louis Hjelmslev"),[[379]](#cite_note-383) [Ferdinand de Saussure](/wiki/Ferdinand_de_Saussure "Ferdinand de Saussure"),[[380]](#cite_note-384) [Winfred P. Lehmann](/wiki/Winfred_P._Lehmann "Winfred P. Lehmann"), [Vladimir Toporov](/wiki/Vladimir_Toporov "Vladimir Toporov")[[381]](#cite_note-385) and others.

There are two main dialects of the Lithuanian language: [Aukštaitian dialect](/wiki/Auk%C5%A1taitian_dialect "Aukštaitian dialect") and [Samogitian dialect](/wiki/Samogitian_dialect "Samogitian dialect"). Aukštaitian dialect is mainly used in the central, southern and eastern parts of Lithuania while Samogitian dialect is used in the western part of the country.[[382]](#cite_note-auto-386) The Samogitian dialect also has many completely different words and is even considered a separate language by some linguists.[[383]](#cite_note-387) Nowadays, the distinguishing feature between the two main Lithuanian dialects is the unequal pronunciation of accented and unaccented two-vowels uo and ie.[[382]](#cite_note-auto-386)

The groundwork for written Lithuanian was laid in 16th and 17th centuries by Lithuanian noblemen and scholars, who promoted Lithuanian language, created dictionaries and published books – [Mikalojus Daukša](/wiki/Mikalojus_Dauk%C5%A1a "Mikalojus Daukša"), [Stanislovas Rapolionis](/wiki/Stanislovas_Rapolionis "Stanislovas Rapolionis"), [Abraomas Kulvietis](/wiki/Abraomas_Kulvietis "Abraomas Kulvietis"), [Jonas Bretkūnas](/wiki/Jonas_Bretk%C5%ABnas "Jonas Bretkūnas"), [Martynas Mažvydas](/wiki/Martynas_Ma%C5%BEvydas "Martynas Mažvydas"), [Konstantinas Sirvydas](/wiki/Konstantinas_Sirvydas "Konstantinas Sirvydas"), Simonas Vaišnoras-Varniškis.[[384]](#cite_note-388)
The first grammar book of the Lithuanian language *Grammatica Litvanica* was published in Latin in 1653 by [Danielius Kleinas](/wiki/Daniel_Klein_(grammarian) "Daniel Klein (grammarian)").

[Jonas Jablonskis](/wiki/Jonas_Jablonskis "Jonas Jablonskis")' works and activities are especially important for the Lithuanian literature moving from the use of dialects to a standard Lithuanian language. The linguistic material which he collected was published in the 20 volumes of [Academic Dictionary of Lithuanian](/wiki/Academic_Dictionary_of_Lithuanian "Academic Dictionary of Lithuanian") and is still being used in research and in editing of texts and books. He also introduced the letter *ū* into Lithuanian writing.[[385]](#cite_note-389)

### Literature

Main article: [Lithuanian literature](/wiki/Lithuanian_literature "Lithuanian literature")

There is a great deal of Lithuanian literature written in [Latin](/wiki/Latin "Latin"), the main scholarly language of the Middle Ages. The edicts of the Lithuanian King [Mindaugas](/wiki/Mindaugas "Mindaugas") are the prime example of the literature of this kind. The [Letters of Gediminas](/wiki/Letters_of_Gediminas "Letters of Gediminas") are another crucial heritage of the Lithuanian Latin writings.

One of the first Lithuanian authors who wrote in Latin was [Nicolaus Hussovianus](/wiki/Miko%C5%82aj_Hussowczyk "Mikołaj Hussowczyk") (around 1480 – after 1533). His poem *Carmen de statura, feritate ac venatione bisontis* (*A Song about the Appearance, Savagery and Hunting of the Bison*), published in 1523, describes the Lithuanian landscape, way of life and customs, touches on some actual political problems, and reflects the clash of paganism and Christianity. A person under the pseudonym [Michalo Lituanus](/wiki/Michalo_Lituanus "Michalo Lituanus") [[lt](https://lt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michalo_Lituanus "lt:Michalo Lituanus")] (around 1490 – 1560) wrote a treatise *[De moribus tartarorum, lituanorum et moscorum](/wiki/De_moribus_tartarorum,_lituanorum_et_moscorum "De moribus tartarorum, lituanorum et moscorum")* (*On the Customs of Tatars, Lithuanians and Muscovites*) in the middle of the 16th century, but it was not published until 1615. An extraordinary figure in the cultural life of Lithuania in the 16th century was the lawyer and poet of Spanish origin Petrus Roysius Maurus Alcagnicensis (around 1505 – 1571). The publicist, lawyer, and mayor of Vilnius, [Augustinus Rotundus](/wiki/Augustinus_Rotundus "Augustinus Rotundus") (around 1520–1582) wrote a no longer existent history of Lithuania in Latin around the year 1560. loannes Radvanus, a humanist poet of the second half of the 16th century, wrote an epic poem imitating the [Aeneid](/wiki/Aeneid "Aeneid") of [Vergil](/wiki/Virgil "Virgil"). His *Radivilias*, intended to become the Lithuanian national epic, was published in Vilnius in 1588.[[387]](#cite_note-391)

17th century Lithuanian scholars also wrote in Latin – [Kazimieras Kojelavičius-Vijūkas](/w/index.php?title=Kazimieras_Kojelavi%C4%8Dius-Vij%C5%ABkas&action=edit&redlink=1 "Kazimieras Kojelavičius-Vijūkas (page does not exist)") [[lt](https://lt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kojelavi%C4%8Dius "lt:Kojelavičius")], [Žygimantas Liauksminas](/wiki/%C5%BDygimantas_Liauksminas "Žygimantas Liauksminas") are known for their Latin writings in theology, rhetorics and music. [Albertas Kojalavičius-Vijūkas](/wiki/Albertas_Kojalavi%C4%8Dius-Vij%C5%ABkas "Albertas Kojalavičius-Vijūkas") wrote first printed Lithuanian history *Historia Lithuania*.

Lithuanian literary works in the [Lithuanian language](/wiki/Lithuanian_language "Lithuanian language") started being first published in the 16th century. In 1547 [Martynas Mažvydas](/wiki/Martynas_Ma%C5%BEvydas "Martynas Mažvydas") compiled and published the first printed Lithuanian book *Katekizmo prasti žodžiai* (*The Simple Words of Catechism*), which marks the beginning of literature, printed in Lithuanian. He was followed by [Mikalojus Daukša](/wiki/Mikalojus_Dauk%C5%A1a "Mikalojus Daukša") with *Katechizmas*. In the 16th and 17th centuries, as in the whole Christian Europe, Lithuanian literature was primarily religious.

The evolution of the old (14th–18th century) Lithuanian literature ends with [Kristijonas Donelaitis](/wiki/Kristijonas_Donelaitis "Kristijonas Donelaitis"), one of the most prominent authors of the [Age of Enlightenment](/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment "Age of Enlightenment"). Donelaitis' poem *Metai* (*[The Seasons](/wiki/The_Seasons_(poem) "The Seasons (poem)")*) is a landmark of the Lithuanian fiction literature, written in [hexameter](/wiki/Hexameter "Hexameter").[[388]](#cite_note-INST-392)

With a mix of [Classicism](/wiki/Classicism "Classicism"), [Sentimentalism](/wiki/Sentimentalism_(literature) "Sentimentalism (literature)") and [Romanticism](/wiki/Romanticism "Romanticism"), the Lithuanian literature of the first half of the 19th century is represented by [Maironis](/wiki/Maironis "Maironis"), [Antanas Baranauskas](/wiki/Antanas_Baranauskas "Antanas Baranauskas"), [Simonas Daukantas](/wiki/Simonas_Daukantas "Simonas Daukantas"), [Oscar Milosz](/wiki/Oscar_Milosz "Oscar Milosz"), and [Simonas Stanevičius](/wiki/Simonas_Stanevi%C4%8Dius "Simonas Stanevičius").[[388]](#cite_note-INST-392) During the Tsarist annexation of Lithuania in the 19th century, the [Lithuanian press ban](/wiki/Lithuanian_press_ban "Lithuanian press ban") was implemented, which led to the formation of the [Knygnešiai](/wiki/Knygne%C5%A1iai "Knygnešiai") (Book smugglers) movement. This movement is thought[*[who?](/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions "Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch")*] to be the very reason the Lithuanian language and literature survived.

20th-century Lithuanian literature is represented by [Juozas Tumas-Vaižgantas](/wiki/Juozas_Tumas-Vai%C5%BEgantas "Juozas Tumas-Vaižgantas"), [Antanas Vienuolis](/wiki/Antanas_Vienuolis "Antanas Vienuolis"), [Bernardas Brazdžionis](/wiki/Bernardas_Brazd%C5%BEionis "Bernardas Brazdžionis"), [Antanas Škėma](/wiki/Antanas_%C5%A0k%C4%97ma "Antanas Škėma"), [Balys Sruoga](/wiki/Balys_Sruoga "Balys Sruoga"), [Vytautas Mačernis](/wiki/Vytautas_Ma%C4%8Dernis "Vytautas Mačernis") and [Justinas Marcinkevičius](/wiki/Justinas_Marcinkevi%C4%8Dius "Justinas Marcinkevičius").[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*]

In 21st century debuted [Kristina Sabaliauskaitė](/wiki/Kristina_Sabaliauskait%C4%97 "Kristina Sabaliauskaitė"), Renata Šerelytė, Valdas Papievis, [Laura Sintija Černiauskaitė](/wiki/Laura_Sintija_%C4%8Cerniauskait%C4%97 "Laura Sintija Černiauskaitė"), [Rūta Šepetys](/wiki/Ruta_Sepetys "Ruta Sepetys").[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*]

### Architecture

See also: [Lithuanian design](/wiki/Lithuanian_design "Lithuanian design")

Several [famous Lithuania-related architects](/wiki/List_of_architects_from_Lithuania "List of architects from Lithuania") are notable for their achievements in the field of architecture. [Johann Christoph Glaubitz](/wiki/Johann_Christoph_Glaubitz "Johann Christoph Glaubitz"), [Marcin Knackfus](/wiki/Marcin_Knackfus "Marcin Knackfus"), [Laurynas Gucevičius](/wiki/Laurynas_Gucevi%C4%8Dius "Laurynas Gucevičius") and [Karol Podczaszyński](/wiki/Karol_Podczaszy%C5%84ski "Karol Podczaszyński") were instrumental in introducing [Baroque](/wiki/Baroque_architecture "Baroque architecture") and [neoclassical](/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture "Neoclassical architecture") architectural movements to the Lithuanian architecture during the seventeenth to nineteenth centuries.[[389]](#cite_note-393) [Vilnius](/wiki/Vilnius "Vilnius") is considered as a capital of the Eastern Europe Baroque.[[390]](#cite_note-394) [Vilnius Old Town](/wiki/Vilnius_Old_Town "Vilnius Old Town") that is full of astonishing Baroque churches and other buildings is a [UNESCO World Heritage Site](/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site "UNESCO World Heritage Site").[[391]](#cite_note-395)

Lithuania is also known for [numerous castles](/wiki/List_of_castles_in_Lithuania "List of castles in Lithuania"). About twenty castles exist in Lithuania. Some castles had to be rebuilt or survive partially. Many [Lithuanian nobles](/wiki/Lithuanian_nobility "Lithuanian nobility")' historic [palaces and manor houses](/wiki/List_of_palaces_and_manor_houses_in_Lithuania "List of palaces and manor houses in Lithuania") have remained till the nowadays and were reconstructed.[[392]](#cite_note-396) Lithuanian village life has existed since the days of [Vytautas the Great](/wiki/Vytautas_the_Great "Vytautas the Great"). [Zervynos](/wiki/Zervynos "Zervynos") and [Kapiniškiai](/wiki/Kapini%C5%A1kiai "Kapiniškiai") are two of many [ethnographic villages](/wiki/Ethnographic_village "Ethnographic village") in Lithuania.[[393]](#cite_note-397) [Rumšiškės](/wiki/Rum%C5%A1i%C5%A1k%C4%97s "Rumšiškės") is an open space museum where old ethnographic architecture is preserved.

During the [interwar period](/wiki/Interwar_period "Interwar period"), [Art Deco](/wiki/Art_Deco "Art Deco"), Lithuanian National Romanticism architectural style buildings were constructed in the Lithuania's temporary capital [Kaunas](/wiki/Kaunas "Kaunas"). Its architecture is regarded as one of the finest examples of the European Art Deco and has received the [European Heritage Label](/wiki/European_Heritage_Label "European Heritage Label").[[394]](#cite_note-398)

### Arts and museums

Main article: [List of museums in Lithuania](/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Lithuania "List of museums in Lithuania")

The [Lithuanian Art Museum](/wiki/Lithuanian_Art_Museum "Lithuanian Art Museum") was founded in 1933 and is the largest museum of art conservation and display in Lithuania.[[395]](#cite_note-399) Among other important museums are the [Palanga Amber Museum](/wiki/Palanga_Amber_Museum "Palanga Amber Museum"), where [amber](/wiki/Amber "Amber") pieces comprise a major part of the collection, National Gallery of Art, presenting collection of Lithuanian art of the 20th and 21st century, [National Museum of Lithuania](/wiki/National_Museum_of_Lithuania "National Museum of Lithuania") presenting Lithuanian archaeology, history and ethnic culture. In 2018 two private museums were opened – [MO Museum](/wiki/MO_Museum "MO Museum") devoted to modern and contemporary Lithuanian art and *Tartle*,[[396]](#cite_note-400) exhibiting a collection of Lithuanian art heritage and artefacts.

Perhaps the most renowned figure in Lithuania's art community was the composer [Mikalojus Konstantinas Čiurlionis](/wiki/Mikalojus_Konstantinas_%C4%8Ciurlionis "Mikalojus Konstantinas Čiurlionis") (1875–1911), an internationally renowned musician. The [2420 Čiurlionis](/wiki/2420_%C4%8Ciurlionis "2420 Čiurlionis") asteroid, identified in 1975, honors his achievements. The [M. K. Čiurlionis National Art Museum](/wiki/M._K._%C4%8Ciurlionis_National_Art_Museum "M. K. Čiurlionis National Art Museum"), as well as the only military museum in Lithuania, [Vytautas the Great War Museum](/wiki/Vytautas_the_Great_War_Museum "Vytautas the Great War Museum"), are located in Kaunas.
[Franciszek Smuglewicz](/wiki/Franciszek_Smuglewicz "Franciszek Smuglewicz"), [Jan Rustem](/wiki/Jan_Rustem "Jan Rustem"), [Józef Oleszkiewicz](/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Oleszkiewicz "Józef Oleszkiewicz") and [Kanuty Rusiecki](/wiki/Kanuty_Rusiecki "Kanuty Rusiecki") are the most prominent Lithuanian painters of the 18th and 19th centuries.[[397]](#cite_note-401)

### Theatre

Lithuania has theatres in [Vilnius](/wiki/Vilnius "Vilnius"), [Kaunas](/wiki/Kaunas "Kaunas"), [Klaipėda](/wiki/Klaip%C4%97da "Klaipėda") and [Panevėžys](/wiki/Panev%C4%97%C5%BEys "Panevėžys"). These include [Lithuanian National Drama Theatre](/wiki/Lithuanian_National_Drama_Theatre "Lithuanian National Drama Theatre"), *[Keistuolių teatras](/wiki/Keistuoli%C5%B3_Teatras "Keistuolių Teatras")* (Theatre of Freaks) in Vilnius, [Kaunas State Drama Theatre](/wiki/Kaunas_State_Drama_Theatre "Kaunas State Drama Theatre"), Theatre of Oskaras Koršunovas, Klaipėda Drama Theatre, Theatre of [Gytis Ivanauskas](/wiki/Gytis_Ivanauskas "Gytis Ivanauskas"), Miltinis Drama Theatre in Panevėžys, The Doll's Theatre, [Old Theatre of Vilnius](/wiki/Old_Theatre_of_Vilnius "Old Theatre of Vilnius").[[398]](#cite_note-402) Theatre festivals include *Sirenos* (Sirens), *TheATRIUM*, *Nerk į teatrą* (Dive into the Theatre).[[399]](#cite_note-403)[[400]](#cite_note-404)[[401]](#cite_note-405)

Lithuanian theatre directors include [Eimuntas Nekrošius](/wiki/Eimuntas_Nekro%C5%A1ius "Eimuntas Nekrošius"), [Jonas Vaitkus](/wiki/Jonas_Vaitkus "Jonas Vaitkus"), Cezaris Graužinis, Gintaras Varnas, [Dalia Ibelhauptaitė](/wiki/Dalia_Ibelhauptait%C4%97 "Dalia Ibelhauptaitė") and Artūras Areima. Actors include Dainius Gavenonis, Rolandas Kazlas, Saulius Balandis and Gabija Jaraminaitė.[[402]](#cite_note-406)

Theatre director [Oskaras Koršunovas](/wiki/Oskaras_Kor%C5%A1unovas "Oskaras Koršunovas") was awarded the Swedish Commander Grand Cross – the [Order of the Polar Star](/wiki/Order_of_the_Polar_Star "Order of the Polar Star").[[403]](#cite_note-407)

### Cinema

Main article: [Cinema of Lithuania](/wiki/Cinema_of_Lithuania "Cinema of Lithuania")

On 28 July 1896, [Thomas Edison](/wiki/Thomas_Edison "Thomas Edison") live photography session was held in the Concerts Hall of the [Botanical Garden of Vilnius University](/wiki/Botanical_Garden_of_Vilnius_University "Botanical Garden of Vilnius University"). After a year, similar American movies were available with the addition of special [phonograph records](/wiki/Phonograph_record "Phonograph record") that also provided sound. In 1909, Lithuanian cinema pioneers [Antanas Račiūnas](/wiki/Antanas_Ra%C4%8Di%C5%ABnas "Antanas Račiūnas") and [Ladislas Starevich](/wiki/Ladislas_Starevich "Ladislas Starevich") released their first movies. Soon the Račiūnas' recordings of Lithuania's views became very popular among the [Lithuanian Americans](/wiki/Lithuanian_Americans "Lithuanian Americans") abroad. In 1925, Pranas Valuskis filmed movie *Naktis Lietuvoje* (Night in Lithuania) about [Lithuanian book smugglers](/wiki/Lithuanian_book_smugglers "Lithuanian book smugglers") that left the first bright Lithuanian footprint in [Hollywood](/wiki/Hollywood_(film_industry) "Hollywood (film industry)"). The most significant and mature Lithuanian American movie of the time *Aukso žąsis* (Golden goose) was created in 1965 by [Birutė Pūkelevičiūtė](/w/index.php?title=Birut%C4%97_P%C5%ABkelevi%C4%8Di%C5%ABt%C4%97&action=edit&redlink=1 "Birutė Pūkelevičiūtė (page does not exist)") [[lt](https://lt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Birut%C4%97_P%C5%ABkelevi%C4%8Di%C5%ABt%C4%97 "lt:Birutė Pūkelevičiūtė")] that featured motifs from the [Brothers Grimm](/wiki/Brothers_Grimm "Brothers Grimm") fairy tales. In 1940, [Romuva Cinema](/wiki/Romuva_Cinema "Romuva Cinema") was opened in [Kaunas](/wiki/Kaunas "Kaunas") and currently is the oldest still operational cinema in Lithuania. After the occupation of the state, movies mostly were used for the [Soviet propaganda](/wiki/Soviet_propaganda "Soviet propaganda") purposes, nevertheless Almantas Grikevičius, Gytis Lukšas, Henrikas Šablevičius, Arūnas Žebriūnas, Raimondas Vabalas were able to overcome the obstacles and create valuable films. After the restoration of the independence, [Šarūnas Bartas](/wiki/%C5%A0ar%C5%ABnas_Bartas "Šarūnas Bartas"), [Audrius Stonys](/wiki/Audrius_Stonys "Audrius Stonys"), [Arūnas Matelis](/wiki/Ar%C5%ABnas_Matelis "Arūnas Matelis"), Audrius Juzėnas, [Algimantas Puipa](/wiki/Algimantas_Puipa "Algimantas Puipa"), [Janina Lapinskaitė](/w/index.php?title=Janina_Lapinskait%C4%97&action=edit&redlink=1 "Janina Lapinskaitė (page does not exist)") [[lt](https://lt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Janina_Lapinskait%C4%97 "lt:Janina Lapinskaitė")], Dijana and her husband Kornelijus Matuzevičius received success in international movie festivals.[[404]](#cite_note-408)

In 2018, 4,265,414 cinema tickets were sold in Lithuania with the average price of €5.26.[[405]](#cite_note-409)

### Music

Main article: [Music of Lithuania](/wiki/Music_of_Lithuania "Music of Lithuania")

See also: [Lithuanian folk music](/wiki/Lithuanian_folk_music "Lithuanian folk music")

Lithuanians dancing at *Skamba skamba kankliai* festival and singing at [Lithuanian Song and Dance Festival](/wiki/Lithuanian_Song_Festival "Lithuanian Song Festival") in [Vingis Park](/wiki/Vingis_Park "Vingis Park")

Lithuanian folk music belongs to [Baltic](/wiki/Baltic_languages "Baltic languages") music branch which is connected with [Neolithic](/wiki/Neolithic "Neolithic") [corded ware](/wiki/Corded_ware "Corded ware") culture. Two instrument cultures meet in the areas inhabited by Lithuanians: stringed ([kanklių](/wiki/Kankl%C4%97s "Kanklės")) and wind instrument cultures. Lithuanian folk music is archaic, mostly used for ritual purposes, containing elements of [paganism](/wiki/Paganism "Paganism") faith. There are three ancient styles of singing in Lithuania connected with ethnographical regions: [monophony](/wiki/Monophony "Monophony"), [heterophony](/wiki/Heterophony "Heterophony") and [polyphony](/wiki/Polyphony "Polyphony"). Folk song genres: Sutartinės (Multipart Songs),[[406]](#cite_note-410) Wedding Songs, War-Historical Time Songs, Calendar Cycle and Ritual Songs and Work Songs.[[407]](#cite_note-411)

Italian artists organized the first [opera](/wiki/Opera "Opera") in Lithuania on 4 September 1636 at the [Palace of the Grand Dukes](/wiki/Palace_of_the_Grand_Dukes_of_Lithuania "Palace of the Grand Dukes of Lithuania") by the order of [Władysław IV Vasa](/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_IV_Vasa "Władysław IV Vasa").[[408]](#cite_note-412) Currently, operas are staged at the [Lithuanian National Opera and Ballet Theatre](/wiki/Lithuanian_National_Opera_and_Ballet_Theatre "Lithuanian National Opera and Ballet Theatre") and also by independent troupe [Vilnius City Opera](/wiki/Vilnius_City_Opera "Vilnius City Opera").

[Mikalojus Konstantinas Čiurlionis](/wiki/Mikalojus_Konstantinas_%C4%8Ciurlionis "Mikalojus Konstantinas Čiurlionis") was a Lithuanian painter and composer. During his short life he created about 200 pieces of music. His works have influenced modern Lithuanian culture. His [symphonic poems](/wiki/Symphonic_poem "Symphonic poem") *In the Forest* (*Miške*) and *The Sea* (*Jūra*) were performed only [posthumously](/wiki/Posthumous_work "Posthumous work"). Čiurlionis contributed to symbolism and art nouveau and was representative of the fin de siècle epoch. He has been considered one of the pioneers of abstract art in Europe.[[409]](#cite_note-413)

In Lithuania, [choral music](/wiki/Choral_music "Choral music") is important. [Vilnius](/wiki/Vilnius "Vilnius") is the only city with three choirs laureates (Brevis, Jauna Muzika and Chamber Choir of the Conservatoire) at the [European Grand Prix for Choral Singing](/wiki/European_Grand_Prix_for_Choral_Singing "European Grand Prix for Choral Singing").[[410]](#cite_note-414) There is a long-standing tradition of the *Dainų šventė* ([Lithuanian Song and Dance Festival](/wiki/Lithuanian_Song_Festival "Lithuanian Song Festival")). The first one took place in [Kaunas](/wiki/Kaunas "Kaunas") in 1924. Since 1990, the festival has been organised every four years and summons roughly 30,000 singers and folk dancers of various professional levels and age groups from across the country.[[411]](#cite_note-415) In 2008, Lithuanian Song and Dance Festival together with its [Latvian](/wiki/Latvian_Song_and_Dance_Festival "Latvian Song and Dance Festival") and [Estonian](/wiki/Estonian_Song_Festival "Estonian Song Festival") versions was inscribed as UNESCO [Masterpiece of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity](/wiki/Masterpieces_of_the_Oral_and_Intangible_Heritage_of_Humanity "Masterpieces of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity").[[412]](#cite_note-416) *Gatvės muzikos diena* (Street Music Day) gathers musicians of various genres annually.[[413]](#cite_note-417)

Modern classical composers emerged in seventies – [Bronius Kutavičius](/wiki/Bronius_Kutavi%C4%8Dius "Bronius Kutavičius"), [Feliksas Bajoras](/w/index.php?title=Feliksas_Bajoras&action=edit&redlink=1 "Feliksas Bajoras (page does not exist)") [[lt](https://lt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feliksas_Bajoras "lt:Feliksas Bajoras")], [Osvaldas Balakauskas](/wiki/Osvaldas_Balakauskas "Osvaldas Balakauskas"), [Onutė Narbutaitė](/wiki/Onut%C4%97_Narbutait%C4%97 "Onutė Narbutaitė"), [Vidmantas Bartulis](/wiki/Vidmantas_Bartulis "Vidmantas Bartulis") and others. Most of those composers explored archaic Lithuanian music and its harmonic combination with modern minimalism and neoromanticism.[[414]](#cite_note-418)

Jazz scene was active even during the years of Soviet occupation. In 1970–71 the Ganelin/Tarasov/Chekasin trio established the Vilnius Jazz School.[[415]](#cite_note-419) Most known annual events are [Vilnius Jazz Festival](/wiki/Vilnius_Jazz_Festival "Vilnius Jazz Festival"), [Kaunas Jazz](/wiki/Kaunas_Jazz "Kaunas Jazz"), Birštonas Jazz.
[Music Information Centre Lithuania](/wiki/Music_Information_Centre_Lithuania "Music Information Centre Lithuania") (MICL) collects, promotes and shares information on Lithuanian musical culture.

#### Rock and protest music

Main article: [Rock music in Lithuania](/wiki/Rock_music_in_Lithuania "Rock music in Lithuania")

After the [Soviet reoccupation of Lithuania in 1944](/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_the_Baltic_states_(1944) "Soviet occupation of the Baltic states (1944)"), the [Soviet's censorship](/wiki/Censorship_in_the_Soviet_Union "Censorship in the Soviet Union") continued firmly controlling all artistic expressions in Lithuania, and any violations by criticizing the regime would immediately result in punishments.[[416]](#cite_note-420) The first local rock bands started to emerge around 1965 and included *Kertukai*, *Aitvarai* and *Nuogi ant slenksčio* in Kaunas, and [Kęstutis Antanėlis](/wiki/K%C4%99stutis_Antan%C4%97lis "Kęstutis Antanėlis"), *Vienuoliai*, and *Gėlių Vaikai* in Vilnius, among others. Unable to express their opinions directly, the Lithuanian artists began organizing patriotic [Roko Maršai](/wiki/Roko_mar%C5%A1as "Roko maršas") and were using [metaphors](/wiki/Metaphor "Metaphor") in their songs' lyrics, which were easily identified for their true meanings by the locals.[[417]](#cite_note-421)[[418]](#cite_note-422) [Postmodernist](/wiki/Postmodernist "Postmodernist") [rock](/wiki/Rock_music "Rock music") band [Antis](/wiki/Antis_(band) "Antis (band)") and its vocalist [Algirdas Kaušpėdas](/wiki/Algirdas_Kau%C5%A1p%C4%97das "Algirdas Kaušpėdas") were one of the most active performers who mocked the Soviet regime by using metaphors. For example, in the song *Zombiai* (Zombies), the band indirectly sang about the [Red Army](/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army") soldiers who occupied the state and its military base in [Ukmergė](/wiki/Ukmerg%C4%97 "Ukmergė").[[419]](#cite_note-423)[[420]](#cite_note-424) [Vytautas Kernagis](/wiki/Vytautas_Kernagis "Vytautas Kernagis")' song *Kolorado vabalai* ([Colorado beetles](/wiki/Colorado_potato_beetle "Colorado potato beetle")) was also a favourite due to its lyrics in which true meaning of the Colorado beetles was intended to be the Soviets decorated with the [Ribbons of Saint George](/wiki/Ribbon_of_Saint_George "Ribbon of Saint George").[[421]](#cite_note-425)

In the early independence years, rock band [Foje](/wiki/Foje "Foje") was particularly popular and gathered tens of thousands of spectators to the concerts.[[422]](#cite_note-426) After disbanding in 1997, Foje vocalist [Andrius Mamontovas](/wiki/Andrius_Mamontovas "Andrius Mamontovas") remained one of the most prominent Lithuanian performers and an active participant in various [charity](/wiki/Charity_(practice) "Charity (practice)") events.[[423]](#cite_note-427) [Marijonas Mikutavičius](/wiki/Marijonas_Mikutavi%C4%8Dius "Marijonas Mikutavičius") is famous for creating unofficial Lithuania sport anthem *Trys milijonai* (Three millions) and official anthem of the [EuroBasket 2011](/wiki/EuroBasket_2011 "EuroBasket 2011") *Nebetyli sirgaliai* (English version was named *Celebrate Basketball*).[[424]](#cite_note-428)[[425]](#cite_note-429)

### Cuisine

Main article: [Lithuanian cuisine](/wiki/Lithuanian_cuisine "Lithuanian cuisine")

Lithuanian cuisine features the products suited to the cool and [moist](/wiki/Maritime_climate "Maritime climate") [northern climate](/wiki/Continental_climate "Continental climate") of Lithuania: [barley](/wiki/Barley "Barley"), [potatoes](/wiki/Potato "Potato"), [rye](/wiki/Rye "Rye"), [beets](/wiki/Beet "Beet"), greens, berries, and [mushrooms](/wiki/Mushroom "Mushroom") are locally grown, and dairy products are one of its specialties. [Fish](/wiki/Fish "Fish") dishes are very popular in the coastal region.[[426]](#cite_note-430) Since it shares its climate and agricultural practices with Northern Europe, Lithuanian cuisine has some similarities to [Scandinavian cuisine](/wiki/Scandinavian_cuisine "Scandinavian cuisine"). Nevertheless, it has its own distinguishing features, which were formed by a variety of influences during the country's long and difficult history.

Dairy products are an important part of traditional Lithuanian cuisine. These include white cottage cheese (*varškės sūris*), curd (*varškė*), soured milk (*rūgpienis*), sour cream (*grietinė*), butter (*sviestas*), and sour cream butter *kastinis*. Traditional meat products are usually seasoned, matured and smoked – smoked sausages (*dešros*), lard (*lašiniai*), *[skilandis](/wiki/Skilandis "Skilandis")*, smoked ham (*kumpis*). Soups (*sriubos*) – boletus soup (*baravykų sriuba*), cabbage soup (*kopūstų sriuba*), beer soup (*alaus sriuba*), milk soup (*pieniška sriuba*), cold-beet soup (*šaltibarščiai*) and various kinds of porridges (*košės*) are part of tradition and daily diet. Freshwater fish, herring, wild berries and mushrooms, honey are highly popular diet to this day.[[427]](#cite_note-431)[[428]](#cite_note-432)

One of the oldest and most fundamental Lithuanian food products was and is rye bread. Rye bread is eaten every day for breakfast, lunch and dinner. Bread played an important role in family rituals and agrarian ceremonies.[[429]](#cite_note-433)

Lithuanians and other nations that once formed part of the [Grand Duchy of Lithuania](/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania "Grand Duchy of Lithuania") share many dishes and beverages. [German traditions](/wiki/German_cuisine "German cuisine") also influenced Lithuanian cuisine, introducing pork and potato dishes, such as potato pudding (*kugelis* or kugel) and [potato sausages](/wiki/Kishka_(food) "Kishka (food)") (*vėdarai*), as well as the baroque tree cake known as *[Šakotis](/wiki/%C5%A0akotis "Šakotis")*. The most exotic of all the influences is Eastern (Karaite) cuisine – the *[kibinai](/wiki/Kibinai "Kibinai")* are popular in Lithuania. Lithuanian noblemen usually hired French chefs, so [French cuisine](/wiki/French_cuisine "French cuisine") influence came to Lithuania in this way.[[430]](#cite_note-434)

[Balts](/wiki/Balts "Balts") were using [mead](/wiki/Mead "Mead") (*[midus](/wiki/Midus "Midus")*) for thousands of years.[[431]](#cite_note-435) Beer (*alus*) is the most common alcoholic beverage. Lithuania has a long farmhouse [beer tradition](/wiki/Beer_in_Lithuania "Beer in Lithuania"), first mentioned in 11th century chronicles. Beer was brewed for ancient Baltic [festivities](/wiki/Festival "Festival") and rituals.[[432]](#cite_note-436) Farmhouse brewing survived to a greater extent in Lithuania than anywhere else, and through accidents of history the Lithuanians then developed a commercial brewing culture from their unique farmhouse traditions.[[433]](#cite_note-437)[[434]](#cite_note-438) Lithuania is top 5 by consumption of beer per capita in Europe in 2015, counting 75 active breweries, 32 of them are microbreweries.[[435]](#cite_note-439) The microbrewery scene in Lithuania has grown, with a number of bars focusing on these beers opening in Vilnius and other parts of the country.[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*]

Eight Lithuanian restaurants are listed in the White Guide Baltic Top 30.[[436]](#cite_note-440) The local „30 geriausių restoranų” guide lists top domestic places,[[437]](#cite_note-441) and Lithuanian restaurants will appear in the [Michelin Guide](/wiki/Michelin_Guide "Michelin Guide") on 13 June 2024.[[438]](#cite_note-442)

### Media

Main article: [Mass media in Lithuania](/wiki/Mass_media_in_Lithuania "Mass media in Lithuania")

The [Constitution of Lithuania](/wiki/Constitution_of_Lithuania "Constitution of Lithuania") provides for [freedom of speech](/wiki/Freedom_of_speech "Freedom of speech") and [press](/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press "Freedom of the press"), and the government generally respects these rights in practice. An independent press, an effective judiciary, and a functioning democratic political system combine to promote these freedoms. However, the constitutional definition of freedom of expression does not protect certain acts, such as incitement to national, racial, religious, or social hatred, violence and discrimination, or slander, and disinformation. It is a crime to deny or "grossly trivialize" Soviet or Nazi German crimes against Lithuania or its citizens, or to deny genocide, [crimes against humanity](/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity "Crimes against humanity"), or [war crimes](/wiki/War_crimes "War crimes").[[439]](#cite_note-443)

In 2021, the best-selling daily national newspapers in Lithuania were *[Lietuvos rytas](/wiki/Lietuvos_rytas "Lietuvos rytas")* (5.4% of all weekly [readers](/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_India_by_readership#Readership_vs_Circulation "List of newspapers in India by readership")), *[Vakaro žinios](/w/index.php?title=Vakaro_%C5%BEinios&action=edit&redlink=1 "Vakaro žinios (page does not exist)") [[lt](https://lt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vakaro_%C5%BEinios "lt:Vakaro žinios")]* (3.2%), *[Kauno diena](/wiki/Kauno_diena "Kauno diena")* (2.9%). Best-selling weekly newspapers were *[Savaitė](/w/index.php?title=Savait%C4%97_(1999)&action=edit&redlink=1 "Savaitė (1999) (page does not exist)") [[lt](https://lt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Savait%C4%97_(1999) "lt:Savaitė (1999)")]* (16.5%), *[Žmonės](/w/index.php?title=%C5%BDmon%C4%97s_(%C5%BEurnalas)&action=edit&redlink=1 "Žmonės (žurnalas) (page does not exist)") [[lt](https://lt.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C5%BDmon%C4%97s_(%C5%BEurnalas) "lt:Žmonės (žurnalas)")]* (8.4%), *Prie kavos* (4.1%), *[Savaitgalis](/wiki/Lietuvos_rytas "Lietuvos rytas")* (3.9%) and *[Verslo žinios](/wiki/Verslo_%C5%BEinios "Verslo žinios")* (3.2%).[[440]](#cite_note-Kantar21-444)

In 2021, the most popular national [television channels](/wiki/Television_channel "Television channel") in Lithuania were [TV3](/wiki/TV3_Lithuania "TV3 Lithuania") (34.6% of the daily audience), [LNK](/wiki/LNK_(television_station) "LNK (television station)") (32.3%), [Lithuanian National Radio and Television](/wiki/Lithuanian_National_Radio_and_Television "Lithuanian National Radio and Television") (31.6%), [BTV](/wiki/BTV_(Lithuania) "BTV (Lithuania)") (17.3%), [Lietuvos rytas TV](/wiki/Lietuvos_rytas_TV "Lietuvos rytas TV") (16.2%), [TV6](/wiki/TV6_(Lithuanian_TV_channel) "TV6 (Lithuanian TV channel)") (15.3%).[[440]](#cite_note-Kantar21-444)

The most popular [radio stations](/wiki/Radio_station "Radio station") in Lithuania were [M-1](/wiki/M-1_(Lithuanian_radio_station) "M-1 (Lithuanian radio station)") (14.5% of daily listeners), *Lietus* (12.7%), *[Radiocentras](/wiki/Radiocentras_(Lithuanian_radio_station) "Radiocentras (Lithuanian radio station)")* (9.1%) and *[LRT Radijas](/wiki/LRT_Radijas "LRT Radijas")* (8.5%).[[440]](#cite_note-Kantar21-444)

### Public holidays and festivals

Main article: [Public holidays in Lithuania](/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Lithuania "Public holidays in Lithuania")

As a result of a thousand-years history, Lithuania has two [National days](/wiki/National_day "National day"). The first one is the [Statehood Day](/wiki/Statehood_Day_(Lithuania) "Statehood Day (Lithuania)") on 6 July, marking the establishment of the medieval [Kingdom of Lithuania](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Lithuania "Kingdom of Lithuania") by [Mindaugas](/wiki/Mindaugas "Mindaugas") in 1253. The creation of modern Lithuanian state is commemorated on 16 February as a [Lithuanian State Reestablishment Day](/wiki/Act_of_Independence_of_Lithuania "Act of Independence of Lithuania") on which declaration of independence from Russia and Germany was declared in 1918. [Joninės](/wiki/Jonin%C4%97s "Joninės") (previously known as *Rasos*) is a public holiday with [paganic](/wiki/Pagan "Pagan") roots that celebrates a [solstice](/wiki/Solstice "Solstice"). As of 2018, there are 13 public holidays (which come with a day off).[[441]](#cite_note-445)

[Kaziuko mugė](/wiki/Kaziuko_mug%C4%97 "Kaziuko mugė") is an annual [fair](/wiki/Fair "Fair") held since the beginning of the 17th century that commemorates the anniversary of [Saint Casimir](/wiki/Saint_Casimir "Saint Casimir")'s death and gathers thousands of visitors and many craftsmen. Other notable festivals are [Vilnius International Film Festival](/wiki/Vilnius_International_Film_Festival "Vilnius International Film Festival"), [Kauno Miesto Diena](/wiki/Kauno_Miesto_Diena "Kauno Miesto Diena"), [Klaipėda Sea Festival](/wiki/Klaip%C4%97da_Sea_Festival "Klaipėda Sea Festival"), [Mados infekcija](/w/index.php?title=Mados_infekcija&action=edit&redlink=1 "Mados infekcija (page does not exist)"), [Vilnius Book Fair](/wiki/Vilnius_Book_Fair "Vilnius Book Fair"), [Vilnius Marathon](/wiki/Vilnius_Marathon "Vilnius Marathon"), [Devilstone Open Air](/wiki/Devilstone_Open_Air "Devilstone Open Air"), [Apuolė 854](/w/index.php?title=Apuol%C4%97_854&action=edit&redlink=1 "Apuolė 854 (page does not exist)") [[lt](https://lt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apuol%C4%97_854 "lt:Apuolė 854")], [Great Žemaičių Kalvarija Festival](/wiki/Great_%C5%BDemai%C4%8Di%C5%B3_Kalvarija_Festival "Great Žemaičių Kalvarija Festival").

| 24 December | [Christmas Eve](/wiki/Christmas_Eve "Christmas Eve") | Kūčios |  |
| 25 and 26 December | [Christmas Day](/wiki/Christmas_Day "Christmas Day") | Kalėdos | Commemorates birth of Jesus. |

### Sports

Main article: [Sport in Lithuania](/wiki/Sport_in_Lithuania "Sport in Lithuania")

[Basketball](/wiki/Basketball "Basketball") is the most popular and [national sport](/wiki/National_sport "National sport") of Lithuania. The [Lithuania national basketball team](/wiki/Lithuania_men%27s_national_basketball_team "Lithuania men's national basketball team") has won the [EuroBasket](/wiki/EuroBasket "EuroBasket") on three occasions ([1937](/wiki/Eurobasket_1937 "Eurobasket 1937"), [1939](/wiki/Eurobasket_1939 "Eurobasket 1939") and [2003](/wiki/Eurobasket_2003 "Eurobasket 2003")), as well a total of 8 other medals in the Eurobasket, the [World Championships](/wiki/FIBA_World_Championship "FIBA World Championship") and the [Olympic Games](/wiki/Basketball_at_the_Summer_Olympics "Basketball at the Summer Olympics"). 76% of the country's population watched the men's national team games live in 2014.[[442]](#cite_note-446) Lithuania hosted the Eurobasket in 1939 and [2011](/wiki/Eurobasket_2011 "Eurobasket 2011"). The historic Lithuanian basketball team [BC Žalgiris](/wiki/BC_%C5%BDalgiris "BC Žalgiris"), from Kaunas, won the European basketball league [Euroleague](/wiki/Euroleague "Euroleague") in 1999. Lithuania has [produced a number](/wiki/List_of_Lithuanian_NBA_players "List of Lithuanian NBA players") of [NBA](/wiki/National_Basketball_Association "National Basketball Association") players, including [Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame](/wiki/Naismith_Memorial_Basketball_Hall_of_Fame "Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame") inductees [Arvydas Sabonis](/wiki/Arvydas_Sabonis "Arvydas Sabonis") and [Šarūnas Marčiulionis](/wiki/%C5%A0ar%C5%ABnas_Mar%C4%8Diulionis "Šarūnas Marčiulionis"),[[443]](#cite_note-447) and current NBA players [Jonas Valančiūnas](/wiki/Jonas_Valan%C4%8Di%C5%ABnas "Jonas Valančiūnas"), [Domantas Sabonis](/wiki/Domantas_Sabonis "Domantas Sabonis").[[444]](#cite_note-448)

Lithuania has won a total of [26 medals at the Olympic Games](/wiki/Lithuania_at_the_Olympics "Lithuania at the Olympics"), including 6 gold medals in [athletics](/wiki/Sport_of_athletics "Sport of athletics"), [modern pentathlon](/wiki/Modern_pentathlon "Modern pentathlon"), [shooting](/wiki/Shooting_sport "Shooting sport"), and [swimming](/wiki/Swimming_(sport) "Swimming (sport)"). Other Lithuanians won Olympic medals representing Soviet Union. [Discus thrower](/wiki/Discus_throw "Discus throw") [Virgilijus Alekna](/wiki/Virgilijus_Alekna "Virgilijus Alekna") is the most successful Olympic athlete of independent Lithuania, having won gold medals in the [2000 Sydney](/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics "2000 Summer Olympics") and [2004 Athens](/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics "2004 Summer Olympics") games, as well as a bronze in [2008 Summer Olympics](/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics "2008 Summer Olympics") and numerous [World Championship](/wiki/IAAF_World_Championships_in_Athletics "IAAF World Championships in Athletics") medals. More recently, a gold medal was won by 15-year-old swimmer [Rūta Meilutytė](/wiki/R%C5%ABta_Meilutyt%C4%97 "Rūta Meilutytė") at the [2012 Summer Olympics](/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics "2012 Summer Olympics") in London, and sparked a rise in popularity for the sport in Lithuania.[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*]

Lithuania hosted the [2021 FIFA Futsal World Cup](/wiki/2021_FIFA_Futsal_World_Cup "2021 FIFA Futsal World Cup"), the first time Lithuania had hosted a FIFA tournament.[[445]](#cite_note-449)

Few Lithuanian athletes have found success in [winter sports](/wiki/Winter_sports "Winter sports"), although facilities are provided by several ice rinks and skiing slopes, including [Snow Arena](/wiki/Snow_Arena "Snow Arena"), the first indoor ski slope in the [Baltics](/wiki/Baltics "Baltics").[[446]](#cite_note-450) In 2018 [Lithuania men's national ice hockey team](/wiki/Lithuania_men%27s_national_ice_hockey_team "Lithuania men's national ice hockey team") won gold medals at the [2018 IIHF World Championship Division I](/wiki/2018_IIHF_World_Championship_Division_I "2018 IIHF World Championship Division I").[[447]](#cite_note-451)

For example, United Nations,[[17]](#cite_note-UN-20) and [Eurovoc](/wiki/Eurovoc "Eurovoc") (which additionally classifies Lithuania as central and eastern European country),[[18]](#cite_note-21) among others, classify it as northern Europe. The [European Commission](/wiki/European_Commission "European Commission"), [European Bank for Reconstruction and Development](/wiki/European_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development "European Bank for Reconstruction and Development") and the [Columbia Encyclopedia](/wiki/Columbia_Encyclopedia "Columbia Encyclopedia") place Lithuania in central Europe.[[19]](#cite_note-22)[[20]](#cite_note-23)[[21]](#cite_note-24) The [CIA World Factbook](/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook "CIA World Factbook")[[22]](#cite_note-CIA-25) classifies it as eastern Europe, and *[Encyclopædia Britannica](/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica "Encyclopædia Britannica")* locates it in northeastern Europe.[[23]](#cite_note-26) Usage varies greatly, and controversially,[[24]](#cite_note-27) in press sources.

Duhamel has developed the approach further: He stresses that the French construction does not correspond to either parliamentary or the presidential form of government, and then develops the distinction of 'système politique' and 'régime constitutionnel'. While the former comprises the exercise of power that results from the dominant institutional practice, the latter is the totality of the rules for the dominant institutional practice of the power. In this way, France appears as 'presidentialist system' endowed with a 'semi-presidential regime' (1983: 587). By this standard he recognizes Duverger's *pléiade* as semi-presidential regimes, as well as Poland, Romania, Bulgaria and Lithuania (1993: 87).

75. **[^](#cite_ref-:0_79-0)** ["Lithuania breaks away from the Soviet Union"](https://www.theguardian.com/world/1990/mar/12/eu.politics). *[The Guardian](/wiki/The_Guardian "The Guardian")*. London. 12 March 1990. [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20190921161738/https://www.theguardian.com/world/1990/mar/12/eu.politics) from the original on 21 September 2019. Retrieved 7 June 2018. Lithuania last night became the first republic to break away from the Soviet Union, by proclaiming the restoration of its pre-war independence. The newly-elected parliament, 'reflecting the people's will,' decreed the restoration of 'the sovereign rights of the Lithuanian state, infringed by alien forces in 1940,' and declared that from that moment Lithuania was again an independent state
76. **[^](#cite_ref-80)** Martha Brill Olcott (1990). ["The Lithuanian Crisis"](https://www.foreignaffairs.com/articles/russian-federation/1990-06-01/lithuanian-crisis). *www.foreignaffairs.com*. [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20210720055455/https://www.foreignaffairs.com/articles/russian-federation/1990-06-01/lithuanian-crisis) from the original on 20 July 2021. Retrieved 18 November 2018. For over two years Lithuania has been moving toward reclaiming its independence. This drive reached a crescendo on 11 March 1990, when the Supreme Soviet of Lithuania declared the republic no longer bound by Soviet law. The act reasserted the independence Lithuania had declared more than seventy years before, a declaration unilaterally annulled by the U.S.S.R. in 1940 when it annexed Lithuania as the result of a pact between Stalin and Hitler.
